=== 1 April.md ===
# 1 April

2024

Stress. One week to the Circo and there’s a lot to do. To be honest a 3-day weekend was the last thing you needed, but there you go. Stress coming from things that are not looking too good (PRIO not paying first trimester, things over budget, spending outside rouanet, no social worker, Erick situation) combined with already low level low level of board confidence.

Stress also from the volume of things that need to be done stacking up in the inbox and the commitments that make it hard to get through them. 

Rafaelzinho playing up in otherwise good banda 1 rehearsal. Timeboxed my way to a pretty productive day and feeling much better having got the majority of the invites out.

=== 1 August.md ===
# 1 August

2024

Just on the plane back after 9 days in the UK. Pottered around Donny with Mum, went for lunch with Pottsie at the Blue Bell in Blaxton and invited everyone to the wedding at family camp. Curry with the boys at the Gurkha place was good although only Chris Barnacoat and Biglad made it for a drink at the Sal afterwards. Sounds like we’ll have Chris Barnacoat and Pottsie and families for the wedding and Stugger and possibly Mark Ellis for Carnaval. Would have liked to met up with Ed Barnard, Chris and Dan to invite them out, but ended up ferrying Oli around after the crash with a motorbike which made it difficult to get that time in London (would have been best to head out early from Donny, have lunch with the boys in London, then head out to Guildford).

One big revelation on the holiday was reading Traction and then Rocket Fuel (now listening to Get a Grip) and discovering a way out of this mess, frankly. The visionary/integrator model gives you a way of getting to reasonable hours without losing your salary, without depriving Favela Brass of your skills, and without freaking the board out. The really big question now is who will do what in the new setup, and especially who will be your integrator. There was a key moment when in the first meeting back, you noticed that Pat was checked out - when you asked her jokingly if she was watching the Olympics, she actually was watching the Olympics. That slowly simmered until the next morning the light came on that you need to open up the integrator role to the field - Pat is now a candidate, no more.

The need for an integrator becomes even more pressing as you look at what’s coming over the next 12 months: starting a new business with Brassify, sorting out the exams for Favela Brass, setting up a trip to New Orleans, looking after a puppy, renovating the house, organising the wedding and possibly even having a baby (Thamires has just taken the goalie off). Brassify is important because the money from that will hopefully mean that Thamires doesn’t have to work at the hospital long-term. It is also the path to the realization of what you set out to achieve, both in terms of Favela Brass and your own artistic ambitions - “provide live music of surpassing quality…” - remember that?

Some big meetings and decisions coming up, no two ways about that. Just remember the rule from the book: *don’t be a weenie!*

2022

Dreamt that Dad left me a little heirloom - a figurine with something vaguely political written on it. Now I know how important those things are.

Long and ultimately satisfying day grinding it out with very little energy after churrasco yesterday. Working on “Stay” and dreaming the grandiose dreams about where brassify could go. 

=== 1 Dec.md ===
# 1 Dec

2024

Not the best day yesterday. In the morning the favela brass concert at the Teatro dos Marionetes with the kids from the schools. You were short on sleeping and didn’t hold back enough from meddling enough. Dude, as far as possible, let them do their thing. You also gave a crap speech, you need to prepare this.

Then in the evening a bad-tempered trip to Leblon with Cacilda. Thamires didn’t want to do it but you dragged her and then berated her the whole time for not giving out enough flyers, which weren’t an effective strategy anyway. Got to the end and we’d made hardly any money. Oh, and there’s hardly any vertical video to do a reel.

You now have to pay the band a minimum along with the hefty uber fees. Need a new strategy here: even a badly paying gig with food is better than this. You do need to build a public, but this isn’t the way. It was a bad day and you could have got the cash out of them better, but it was too far off for it to be worth doing this again.

Late-night is crap for your body clock and not great if there are underage band members. 

Ah, and Geiza was a total dickhead the whole time.

2022

You’ve got it into your head that you’re neurotic. That if you have kids you’ll be on their case the whole time and worrying about everything. Thing is, you just need to look after yourself and you can actually be pretty level-headed.

You, Wesley and Raissa in leadership team with the next hire being a development coordinator who could turn into integrator. A negative PCR test now means I would have had to have contracted COVID in the two days before flying and had it out of my system in 10 days. Unlikely.  A positive test would be rough, but not necessarily the new variant (most likely off Joe and Amélia).

Board meeting was tough today. Just going round in circles trying to get us to the point where we have enough board members for a governance committee. Need to sleep on this to think of a way out.

Oh and playing bergmuller last thing was bliss. More of this please.

=== 1 Jan.md ===
# 1 Jan

*Thought for the day:*

For any musical situation really, there are 3 commandments:

Be prepared
Be on time
Be nice

2023

Our for a meal with Val and Hardy last night in Monmartre. Went out to watch the fireworks and we were looking out the wrong way - shades of Chris Caulfield!

Settled on the Bousquet etudes for this year’s trumpet practice. Maybe 4 months on each set of 12. Looking forward to working on these - who knows maybe even switching over to cornet for a bit.

New Year’s resolution: no caffeinated drinks other than green tea.

What do you want more of in 2023?

Writing and recording brassify arrangements 
Dates / relationships
Socials like the bbq

What do you want less of?

Politics / stress
Bureaucracy / admin

Really you just want and need to get stuck into the arrangements.

2022

Didn’t make it to midnight yesterday. Just me and Mum at home this year. Monique not responding (remember this at Carnaval).

New Years Day Oli’s lot came round and you bought them games. This finally got you out of your head. Great times.

2021

Saw the new year in with Mum and Dad and Jules Holland. Actually find Jules Holland fairly depressing in terms of the lack of decent new music. Reflects how stagnant things have been musically since the 90s. Nothing new of note for at least 20 years, 2020 almost indistinguishable from 2000.

Bought the bass trombone today. Let’s pray for a decent slide. Should I take the plunge and try to get a bari out there so I can record the whole band out there? Or just record when I’m back in the UK now that I have a better idea?

=== 1 November.md ===
# 1 November

2023

PRIO Blues & Jazz Festival at the weekend. Just doing the mini-cortejos inside was a bit of a let down, but playing together with Bloco 442 was great and looks like we have found Henri a gig on trombone.

Monitoring wasn’t up to scratch but the Mums kicked up a ridiculous fuss about nothing. Geiza putting threats about calling lawyers in the Favela Brass group. Spent the whole day today debating with people what to do - take Geiza, Carol and Dani out? Just Geiza? 

Then had Carol and Marquinho round later with Marquinho saying he’s leaving over a stolen toddynho. Just ridiculous. Gave him the story of the boy who cried wolf.

2022

Had a lovely day and a bit in Miguel Pereira staying at Luiz Henrique and Celia’s airbnb. Cycling day on Sunday all round Miguel and Paty then to Vassouras and back. Stunning scenery. Looking at houses yesterday with estate agent Sara who had us chasing the bus down the hill after getting me back late. Very viable looking houses and god can you imagine being able to cycle out into those hills every day?

Airbnb option worth thinking about. Do some maths, get it on a spreadsheet.

Rouanet stuff slightly worrying - whole contrapartida thing suddenly looks more difficult and Fatima just cancels meeting after meeting. How are we going to get the relatórios done if Fatima is just taking our money? Not to mention next year’s project being gridlocked in the Salic system.

Rainy few weeks and Favela Brass attendance is dodgy as a result. Spent my non-time this morning looking at how to step down as ED without stepping down as ED, and think I got it: hire a director for each project who takes all that heat. I just work with the board writing the projects and getting the backers.

Read somewhere that what actually does lead people to behave well is when they are imagining that someone is watching over them. That works for you, and Dad. Hold onto that.

2021

Stressed but not the worst kind of stress. Monique wants to do something when she’s here during November but it’s such a busy time. Ended up settling on a night + day away. Work is important, but so is you finding someone.

That said, you can’t let rouanet slip away. You should be concentrating on just this. Today was your day off so you are forgiven for spending it making the intermediate transposition book (which I think is a big breakthrough) and playing piano. But you’ve got to make strides on this in November. Make that R$40k happen.

=== 10 April.md ===
# 10 April

10 April

2024

Time to start thinking about the wedding! 

**La Prière du Para**

Je m’adresse à vous, mon Dieu, car vous donnez Ce qu’on ne peut obtenir que de soi
Donnez-moi, mon Dieu, ce qui vous reste Donnez-moi ce qu’on ne vous demande jamais.
Je ne vous demande pas le repos, Ni la tranquillité Ni celle de l’âme, ni celle du corps.
Je ne vous demande pas la richesse Ni le succès, ni même la santé.
Tout ça, mon Dieu, on vous le demande tellement Que vous ne devez plus en avoir.
Donnez-moi, mon Dieu, ce qui vous reste Donnez-moi ce que l’on vous refuse.
Je veux l’insécurité et l’inquiétude. Je veux la tourmente et la bagarre
Et que vous me les donniez, mon Dieu, définitivement.
Que je sois sûr de les avoir toujours Car je n’aurai pas toujours le courage De vous les demander.
Donnez-moi, mon Dieu, ce qui vous reste. Donnez-moi ce dont les autres ne veulent pas.
Mais donnez-moi aussi le courage Et la force et la foi.
Car vous seul donnez, mon Dieu, Ce que l’on ne peut attendre que de soi.
Amen.

2021

I’m content to be a bit of an APT: The overly ambitious project that tried to introduce too many innovations on a ridiculously small budget, rushed it all to market, bungled its communications and became a general laughing stock; but also the train that “marked a number of world firsts, including being the first self-propelled active tilting train; the first train to have computer designed wheel-sets and active suspension; and the first train to run at over 100 mph on any track without side-to-side instability.”

Got the name. Projeto aprendendo em harmonia (dot org). Beer earned. Only thing bothering me is that there are 12 different colours of fitas de bonfim. I think go with 12. It puts ABSRM out of the picture. You can still use ABSRM as a guide because, crucially, the final grade will be at the same level. Therefore for your grade 3 you can use ABRSM grade 2 as an example etc. And it makes it Brasil. AND that last grade of a black ribbon with red letters is sexy! rs And 12 times 12 is 144 and is 144 is your favorite number. That is clearly the most important consideration.

47cm of ribbon is a lot, but I want to see a maestro demand that a student cuts their ribbon off. There are going to be memories in these ribbons, exchanges, concerts. Man this is cool. And the name of the project where they learned (or even the teacher) is cool. Imagine a bunch of kids from different projects coming together with the same ribbons but with different project names. V.cool

You need the initial syllabus and you need the governance structure for decisions about changes to the syllabus in the future to be made well. But by God it’s a great idea. I guess you need to think at what point should you start talking to other projects - when syllabus/folhas are done?

Point is, she’s not about the budget or the technical details - she just didn’t like being overruled in terms of the parents coming.

Stuff like that makes you want to move on from Favela Brass, and much though Pam is difficult, so was Carola, so is Cris, so is Sômulo, Mirela, Raissa, Fernando Pereira, Mangueirinha, Bindu, Stugger etc.

You’ll always have to deal with politics, but you don’t have to put yourself in a job where you’re dealing with this level of politics. And you have to recognise when a situation is toxic, like at the British School.

The question is: how would you make your money away from Favela Brass?

2025

Would have liked to pay more to cover their expenses but just too strapped at the moment as the building work rages on and other things keep coming in (fridge, bomba for swimming pool, etc.)

Wasn’t sleeping well at all in the run up to Carnaval - not only because of the uncertainties of taking Cacilda to Carnival, but also with the delay for the Rouanet cash to be transferred to the conta de movimentação, and then us not getting out Rouanet prestação de contas in in time.

Seems like you have flattened your belly quite a bit with this running the Caminho de Darwin most days lark. Keep it up!

2021

Full day, straight into making rhythm reading videos and tests which I think are turning out great. Busy coordinating video projects with projeto Guri and Leandro’s school - would be fantastic to cement those partnerships. 

Had the idea of separating out the method and calling it Banda Karate. Gives you independence from the project, makes for better website and cleaner Favela Brass YouTube channel. Also means that other projects don’t feel like they are somehow supplicating to the favela brass brand. And you can also make money from it - just do your own Patreon and benfeitoria.

Did the talk for Felipe Mello - went great, who knows some more regional exchange partners.

First governance meeting was interesting. Sômulo is up for chairing it (is leaving APE) and the key tasks list generated some interesting conversation - Angelo not at all keen on anything that sounds like the Governance committee evaluating the performance of the board and effectiveness of meetings and me and Sômulo pushing back.

10th December

2020

Stu Macdonald’s instruments have come and I’m busy recording the first big band arrangement: bang. A slightly depressing feeling came over me, which was that all that time and energy I wasted with “MLT” in the mornings could have been employed so much better just writing arrangements. One ship drives East, another west
By the self same gale that blows
Tis the set of the sail and not the Gale
That determines the way she goes

The heights by great men reached and kept
Were not attained by sudden flight 
But they while their companions slept

=== 11 April.md ===
# 11 April

11 April

2022

First Cacilda at cozinha da lapa yesterday. Went well in the end. Messy jam with too many drummers and not enough horns, but the New Orleans stuff with Marquinho and Bolinho really shone. Now to try and push things in the direction of having a half decent band at some point in the proceedings.

Watching Fargo series which is great. 

2021

Forgot to say yesterday that after running up to the top I stopped at around sunset on the secluded rock on the way down and listened to take it to the limit on the headphones. Imagined kids all over the city practicing away with fitas dangling from their instruments. Very cheesy, but still a nice thought.

Things I’m grateful for. The taste of an ice-cold beer. The satisfaction of playing piano with the metronome. Living in a community.

You spent the best part of your 20s fairly alone. Not a complete hermit, but not a proper social life. You would have loved to live where everyone knows your name, knows what you are about, with local restaurants etc. Teaching the local kids to play music and then having them as your friends when they get older. It’s magic. It’s not perfect. But it’s magic.

Worrying a bit about the fact that I told Joe, in an unguarded moment, that Stugger and Carola splitting would be good news for me because I would get my friend back. Joe, like Tom Le Mesurier (and most people!), has got a big mouth, and could well pass this on to Raissa while they are out drinking. === 11 July.md ===
# 11 July 

2023

Pam berates you and Cris for 10 minutes straight on zoom for being the root cause of all of the problems in the project and then you both meekly apologize.

Think.

You want to get away from her, but you can’t fire her. She’s just so incredibly structured - once she gets a hold of something that’s it, you can’t work on it together. It’s how she sees it and anything from you is just wrong. Think budgets, RACI, events.

But the overall dynamic is one of the split leadership that doesn’t work. You end up with 2 projects. If it wasn’t her, it would be someone else. And you don’t have the time to do justice the ED role because you’re busy writing arrangements and teaching.

The board are afraid of change, and they are afraid of employees. The idea of the meetings without you is scary, because they have no North and would be worried about making mistakes. You AND Pam in meetings is far from ideal, but maybe it is the only way to bridge over to Pam.

*Pois é, podemos pensar num programa de transição, de repente deixar ela cuidando da gerência agora, no segundo semestre passar a te acompanhar em algumas coisas, lá pra outubro ir tomando frente com sua supervisão e quem sabe no projeto 2024 ela assumir*

But but but… do you want to leave FB with Pam? If the directors get used to her they won’t want to change her and you’ll be dealing with her as long as you’re with FB. Would it not be better to just see this year’s contract out before handing over more power to her?

If you were to dare to dream now, you would be in your own house in Engenho do Mato with Thamires and family. You’d have a bunch of cash coming in from Airbnb, you’d be working everyday in your studio on Brassify arrangements, and Favela Brass would be there on the other side of the water running without you.

Every couple of weeks you’d go to Pereira to see the kids play, or do a gig at Hedi’s.

How to get there…

Get 19B ready to rent out long-term. Especially the roof. Or sell it!

Get Pam reporting to the board and lose the ED responsibilities.

Before that, for 2024 this looks like a pretty nice job description.

« Profissional responsável pelo lado artístico no projeto: organização das bandas, coordenação de professores, avaliação dos alunos, curadoria do repertório, produção de arranjos, regência em apresentações, elaboração do programa de estudo, desenvolvimento dos recursos ensino à distância, incluindo os recursos para alunos portadores de deficiência. »

By the way 3 green teas is still too much.

=== 11 March.md ===
# 11 March

2025

Piano practice works best when you view it primarily as concentration practice, and the way to do that is through the zero-tolerance thing. As in meditation, where you lose focus on the breath and come back, so in piano practice you lose focus on the piano (as evidenced by a mistake) and then come back (by starting again).

You can practice the part that you got wrong round a few times before you go back, but you want to be spending most of your time walking that tightrope. Focusing on concentration means you learn more, because you are approaching each note with intentionality, knowing that you don’t have the option of trial and error - you have to think things through first.

The flexi-time approach is perfect here - take as much time as you want, just get it right!

=== 11 May.md ===
# 11 May

2025

Listened to the AOM podcast this morning and it was a woman talking about aphorisms to live by. The one that stuck out was “make the choice that will give you a bigger life”. In the last couple of years I think you have done that: proposed to Thamires, adopted Zola, had Thiago, bought a house, delegated the day-to-day of Favela Brass, started Cacilda. The first thing that struck you when you heard that was to think about the Street Music World Cup. That’s definitely bigger than slowly getting Favela Brass running on rails and gigging with Cacilda.

That said, you just wrote your first original tune for Cacilda. That’s big. If this is about really saving live music then having something genuinely fresh, not just arrangements of classic tunes, makes the whole thing more vital. So the writing still has to be a part of it. You need to have 90 mins a day for writing and that has to start sooner rather than later. But this needs to be more than you cutting yourself off and writing a bunch of arrangements for a YouTube channel that doesn’t get noticed, and you can’t end up organising the logistics of Cacilda doing wedding gigs.

AI is here and there must be a way that this can give you a bigger life. It handles the small stuff and with everyday that passes it handles bigger stuff. Bigger I think does have to include you actually making some money. A big life isn’t one where you’re borrowing money from your Mum; a big life isn’t now where Thamires has to work as a hospital admin to pay for our health insurance. Although the biography of Jensen Huang comes with a generous helping of survivor bias, it does show that part of the role of a leader is to have the balls to go for things, rather than playing it safe.

I think that between making AI tools to automate music teaching and doing the street brass World Cup, the latter would perhaps be the bigger choice as the main focus. We should be developing the best tools we can at Favela Brass for enhancing the lessons, but perhaps better to wait a bit, because what Claude quoted as a million-dollar 2-year project in 2025 will only decrease in terms of price and timescale as time goes on.

Biggest worry about the street brass World Cup is that Favela Brass goes off the boil in the meantime. But you have AI now and the first Copa da Cacilda is next year. Plenty of time to supercharge Favela Brass now!

Ding dong with the finance committee last night about advancing money to the staff while we’re waiting for the adequação of Rouanet 2023 to go through. Long and short: Mirela’s too small for the president job; you have a board that loves to whinge about a lack of cash but doesn’t do anything to help bring it in.

Saw the Darcy Ribeiro building today with Pam and her architect friend. Walked back with her to her house and talked about the executive director thing. Genie’s out of the bottle now. She’s a bit arrogant, doesn’t have much in the way of charisma, and snarls from time to time. But she’ll be a safe pair of hands for Favela Brass. There’s an aspect of you giving up, but you have to ask yourself: is artistic director and executive director viable as the team grows? Is that really best for the project?

Question is: what’s your niche now? If you’re only doing music at Favela Brass you’ll have a bit of time for a sideline or 2: wouldn’t running a band or two and writing arrangements for them be the ticket? I guess the main thing is getting at the Brassify thing. It’s a good idea. Do it right and it’s bigger than Favela Brass. The world needs it, and it could take you anywhere. Go get ‘em, founder.

=== 13 August.md ===
# 13 August

2023

**Tom, don’t go floppy on this one**: you have your chance now to get Pam out with the backing of your team. It’s abrupt, and you will face resistance, but both for Favela Brass and you it is much better that she leaves now - why?

1. The longer she stays, the more she’ll get entrenched - once the current crisis with her and Cris and Raissa blows over inertia may set in.
2. Pat is joining the team - you want to get off on the right foot with her.
3. You want to stay with Favela Brass as artistic director - that could even be something that works indefinitely. But with Pam managing your life would be a misery and she’d be constantly wanting to bulldoze you out. You need to find a Wesley on the admin side - someone who is a joy to deal with (or at least not a complete nightmare)
4. The Executive Director/Project Manager division doesn’t work - it’s one person, and it’s very clear now that you cannot give that power to Pam. You need to get her out to give someone else a chance, or you’re stuck doing 2 jobs forever.
5. Everything she’s doing now is to try and entrench herself and un-entrench other people, like you and Cris. Don’t give her space to manoeuvre, to set up her own team of contacts etc. Imagine if she meets PRIO, etc.
6. The back end of this year is a nice period of time to test someone out - how about this idea of someone working with you as both consultant/assistant?
7. You can’t trust her - think Sômulo, think this meeting with the prefeitura without you right now.
8. Remember Robert Greene - destroy your enemies totally, and also beware the bad apple effect. She’s not respecting you and that is contagioius.
9. You want stability right now - all this stress could see Pat, Cris or Raissa leave and it just goes on. 
10. **She’s making your life a misery and the problem will only get worse, to the point where you would have to leave Favela Brass, or pick up the pieces after she’s run it into a wall.**

2021

Did the right thing. Stayed home and organized for Mangueirinha to do the oficinas. Very relieved. Board is supportive and the logistics look ok. Actually a good exercise to make things work without you.

I think it’s starting to set in for Mum now and it’s going to be very difficult. So glad she wasn’t alone today.

2020

Last day of official quarantine. 10 days no shower or change of clothes. Will be very nice to have a shower, play piano and go for a bike ride tomorrow. Cabin fever starting to set in a little bit here.

Has been good though, recording the first big band charts. Such a great learning opportunity - write/rework charts in the morning, record in the afternoon, etc. Hopefully over the course of the next weeks you’ll pick up the chops to write big band charts without having to hear them recorded and then adjust.

Bang by Anitta took a lot of work, and Blinding lights is also going to have to be changed a lot. But these charts are going to be a real mainstay of the project, and of your career. The videos were good too, but arrangements give everyone - at favela brass and also your exchange partners - a musical roadmap. This is definitely the part of the project that you can do better than others (as opposed to the admin stuff).

The thing to work out is how you’re going to get them played. This jigsaw still needs working out. Fact is that you don’t have a full band of kids ready to play anything other than very very easy big band charts, which yours are not. And in the first stages you want them memorising tunes anyway. Part of this is getting them learning to read rhythms as well, so need to get on that as well.

=== 13 September.md ===
# 13 September

2024

Has the unthinkable happened? **Things that don’t sit right:**

The doctors are putting the conception date for the baby at variously 6 and 8 weeks. That would be 1st of August or 18th of July. You went on the 22nd of July and got back on the 1st. The IUD came out, due to heavy bleeding (which could indicate that it was out of place) on the 25th, one week before you came back. Generally the estimates for conception have been before you got back from the UK.

When Thamires first told you, she was saying that she had been pregnant a week, but that then changed to 5 weeks - could she really have confused that, or was she trying to push the date onto safer ground? 

She took a week to tell you. Working up to it?

The leaves in the pool when you got back. Friday the 26th she was in the hospital. The leaves stacked up in the week after that. You had a gut reaction when you saw those leaves.

She had waxed down below and it felt different. Could be that it felt different because of the wax, or possibly even taking the IUD out, but it felt different. Both the waxing and the different feel are a move away from the baseline.

The photo in lingerie. First photo like that she’s sent you and 30 mins later when you arrived no sign of the lingerie.

Last night at La Mafia when you were on the point of conception dates she said something like “It couldn’t have been before the 25th because it’s impossible to get pregnant with an IUD in”. Not that it couldn’t have been before the 1st because there was no sperm up until that point.

The chances of conceiving on the very 1st attempt are incredibly slim. 

You hadn’t been having sex with her that frequently and went to England without her.

Even though you are clearly asking a lot of questions about the conception date etc. she hasn’t done what you did with the condom packet and taken it straight on, i.e “I know the dates aren’t stacking up but just let me tell you now, this child is yours - I would never cheat on you in a million years.” or even “Are you out of your mind? I can’t even believe that you would question the dates!!” Or “I get it - well if it’s going to be an issue I’ll do a DNA test when it comes out to put your mind at rest”.

She also commented that she didn’t think she could get pregnant straight after taking the IDU out.

**On the other hand:**

“Once you know the first day of your last period, you can add 11 to 21 days to figure out your conception date.” If Thamires was bleeding heavily on the 24th then there’s a good chance she was on her period. 11 to 21 days after that gives 4th to 14th of August, with sex date going back to the 1st which checks out. However that gives 4-6 weeks absolute max for the pregnancy which works with the 6-8 weeks from the doctors, but only just.

Would she be reckless enough to not only have sex with someone else, but to have unprotected sex without an IDU?

Even with the sex life being a bit under par, you still have a strong relationship. 

Until the 25th she had an IDU in, so it’s very unlikely (but not impossible) that the 8-week conception date is correct - that is, even for the hypothesis of her messing around while you’re away, the 18th of July doesn’t stack up.

**What to do?**

Option A - say nothing, do a secret DNA test when the baby is born.

Plusses - won’t mess with relationship
Minuses - rules out abortion in case of mismatch

Option B - ask for a DNA test during pregnancy

Plusses - At 3-4 months there’s still time to abort
Minuses - If it’s yours it’s a massive unnecessary stress and strain on the relationship, and if it isn’t then you would have found out anyway after the birth and would you want to stay with someone who cheats on you? That is, would you even want the option of abortion and starting all over?

Option C - ask her straight out, be open that you’ll be testing

Plusses - It’s honest. If she knows you’ll test and is in doubt about the paternity, she might well come clean. If she’s in no doubt she’ll have the opportunity to emphatically deny.

**Decision**

Do the test for sure, openly or secretly as soon as the baby is born. Get married legally only in 2026.

Get the estimated due date ASAP.

If the dates are blatantly not stacking up, take the opportunity to say “Babes I wouldn’t even dream of doing this if it wasn’t for the fact that the doctors are saying that the baby was conceived when I was in another country, but when the baby is born I’m going to do a DNA test.” And “I hate to ask this question by I feel like I need to ask you straight: have you slept with anyone else apart from me since we’ve been together?”

**Possible outcomes:**

When the baby is born it’s yours and your mind is at rest

When the baby is born it’s not yours and the world comes crashing down, but you’re not legally obliged to support the baby or give up half of the house.

Thamires comes clean about possibility of it not being yours, tests early, aborts or not, get on with life (with our without you).

**Note**
**
**
Something makes me thing that the baby is probably yours but that she may have cheated on you while you were away.

2022

Nasty situation with Samuel. As well as him not going to SP you’ve now taken him out of the band. You didn’t communicate it properly with the parents beforehand and Marlucia is going schitz. You did try to organize a sit-down with Marlucia which she ignored, he’s has fallen behind to the point where it doesn’t make sense for him to be in the same shows/rehearsals, and you gave him a private lesson with Amelia. But you could have handled this better.

We now have a WhatsApp group of the Mums scheming against you, a WhatsApp group and Instagram of the students that you’re not party to and you’re relying on Cris and Mangueirinha to back you up - both of whom are vying for position. Here comes the storm.

Not only this but the São Paulo students are missing lessons without letting me know, so you’re going to have to open up yet another front.

You started the lessons in the school with a view to winding down the lessons in the favela, exactly because of this dynamic. The idiot parents. You can’t stop the lessons in the favela. But you can reduce your own personal investment if needed. Say that you need more time to stay on top of the organization. Reshuffle things a bit.

Have to confess that focusing on results as opposed to moralizing (you should have done this, they shouldn’t have done that, am I a good person etc.) does feel better. Don’t get upset by the games people play, just work out what you need to do. Solve problems.

=== 14 June-1.md ===
# 14 June

Monmartre with Mum. Played pocket trumpet with a gypsy guitarist in the street. Cornet would be better for this kind of thing.

Had a thought. After reading 4,000 weeks you’re worrying that you’re always living for tomorrow. You come to Paris, you start coming up with all sorts of ideas for the future.

But rather than beating yourself up about that, why not think of it in terms of creativity? That is, you’re a creative type, that’s what makes you happy: making music and making music happen. If you can’t dream a bit then what’s the bloody point?

You plan stuff, work on it looking forward, it comes to fruition or goes tits up, on to the next thing. Isn’t what that life’s about?

MLT thought: Learning music is magic. Wouldn’t it be great if you could just sing the scale degree along with the note to understand it all on a musical level? But it’s not like that - it’s much richer and complex and in the end all you can do is take the horse to water every day.

=== 14th Jan.md ===
# 14th Jan

2021

A very happy mistake today. I didn’t get my 30 mins of piano practice done in time, so in my mind I had to “eat into” my leisure time by playing after I’d had the obligatory evening glass of wine at 8pm.

When I started playing (from the new big intermediate classical piano book) I realized that THIS is your leisure pursuit! Not Netflix, not DIY. It just feels so right and you went wrong feeling pretty wretched to being on top of the world. When you knock off THIS IS WHAT YOU DO!

You learn so much every time you go to the piano. This is alive time! This is you. If there’s one thing you would love to conquer it’s the piano. And the classical repertoire is just a joy to play. Not 30 obligatory mins a day, but much more voluntary minutes per day including the evening.

These are the pleasures! Running listening to history, reading history before bed, learning to arrange for big band and sitting at the piano with a cup of tea or a glass of wine. Life is good! This is such a golden time...

Piano could become a sort of meditation practice. It’s concentration, absorption, flow and self-control - no two ways about that.

=== 16 December.md ===
# 16 December

**16 December**
**
**
**DAILY MUSE - DETACHMENT**
**
**
*“If you come across any special trait of meanness or stupidity . . . you must be careful not to let it annoy or distress you, but to look upon it merely as an addition to your knowledge - a new fact to be considered in studying the character of humanity. Your attitude towards it will be that of the mineralogist who stumbles upon a very characteristic specimen of a mineral.”*
*
*
- *Arthur Schopenhauer*

Don’t take it all too seriously. You have been stressing the last few days about all the Favela Brass team coming together for the Christmas pizza at Hedi’s and especially this situation with Marcelo the video guy. On another day it’s the situation with Fernando Pereira, on another day it’s Mangueirinha, or Stugger, and so on. The point is that with enough physical exercise and meditation you can get to a mental space where you can see all this for what it is - a fantastic opportunity for you to learn and grow after many lost years of not dealing with people. Take a step back and learn to love it - it’s all just a fun game, and one that you’ll be much better at if you’re playing with a smile your face.
**
**
**2020**

Today was quite a sparky day. Just come back from a long walk with a new framework for music learning:

ELEMENTS OF MUSICIANSHIP:

1. Imagination

1. Comprehension

1. Technique

WE need to be working up to music learning activities that **feed **the imagination, **sharpen **our comprehension and **cultivate **good technique all at the same time. That’s where Gordon falls down.

IMAGINATION means the generation of meaningful musical ideas. What pops into your “mind’s ear”. Pure unconscious/implicit. Meaningful means ideas that will have an emotional resonance. How compelling and original are your musical thoughts?

COMPREHENSION is how well you can fit musical stimuli into your mental model as a musician. This has parallel and serial conscious/explicit and unconscious/implicit aspects. When you read music and hear the sound in your head, that is comprehension but this on both and explicit and implicit level.

TECHNIQUE is about practical execution. How well can you convert ideas into practical sonic reality through instruments or the voice. How skilfully can you create the desired musical effect? Arranging has a technical aspect in terms of the limitations of the instruments - making something that can be executed smoothly. Habituating high technical standards. Mostly technique is going from explicit actions to implicit habits.

What does all this mean in terms of your course?

Theory is an important part of comprehension (Gordon putting this at the end was silly - all these things run in parallel).

You need to be feeding their imagination with meaningful ideas in a way that they can start to comprehend theoretically as well. Think Oscar Peterson’s piano book.  Each grade from 2 on could have a little 12-bar blues etude that also points to the structure Joe Avery, then more complicated Boogie-Woogie type stuff. 

It means you’re trying to bring it all along together - not leaving any of the elements of musicianship out.

**
**

DAILY NUGGET:

Know yourself. Grandiose, narcissistic people are good at getting into positions of leadership. However they don’t do too well when they are there - and especially not the fragile, neurotic types. When people inevitably take pot shots at them they take it all personally and tend to lash out in ways that bring things crashing down. These people need to meditate and do lots of exercise to keep things in perspective. Probably a good idea to keep the caffeine down as well. In relationships, narcissistic people tend to hurt the people around them through their lack of interest in them. Either find a way to lead with empathy and humility or get out of the kitchen. And get out of your own arse and start taking time out for the people around you.

Another mould you fit into is that of the creative type outlined by Micky Cheeksentmehi. So you’re a highly creative, fragile narcissist then.

2023

The very best thing is when there’s a part of the arrangement that, on listening to the arrangement, you think was actually part of the original even though it isn’t. Case in point: intro to Glamurosa - that’s the sweet spot! Don’t do transcriptions: build new brass band arrangements that capture the spirit of the original, taking whatever liberties necessary to make them work with live instrumentation. Find the key elements to retain.

Been going on long walks and thinking about 3 main things:

1. What to do in terms of stepping down as ED of Favela brass
2. How to get Brassify going
3. Whether to buy a house with inheritance

I think in general it doesn’t make sense to leave Rio, and Santa Teresa is not only close to Favela Brass and the action generally: it’s also a beautiful charming neighborhood and affordable especially in pounds terms.
  
You are wanting to focus more on Brassify so a house with a basement to record in would make a big difference. Really, you need at least an hour for recording every morning. There are other ways to make recording in the morning a possibility:

A. Record at assuncao. 6am? Fiddly, but never know you might get into a rhythm. Give it a try Mon-Fri this week.
B. Set up regular recording session at a studio nearby. Candidates include Bindu’s, Mustafa’s, local studios.
C. Come to a deal with baby Joe whereby you can record at home every day a bit earlier maybe 9:30 (put exercise first).
D. Buy or rent a house with a basement or somewhere you can record.
E. Throw out roommates, possibly soundproof downstairs and just get on with it.
F. Build a custom studio behind house.
G. Improve existing soundproofing within house to make early morning practice ok for residents (brick up window, close door, put door at bottom of steps).

Making brassify work involves getting into an every day writing/recording routine. It also involves promoting it and that may well mean a band in Rio. Think about it.

In terms of stepping down is there a gradual option?

2021

Succumbed to the espresso on the way back to Rio. Read the Josef Lhevinne piano book: “What is so fascinating as the art of music; and how can it be approached with more charm by the individual than through the pianoforte?”

Still haunted by the feeling that I wasn’t there for Dad at the end. And that I didn’t “hold my end up”. 40 could have been the denouement. You could have been earning well with a flourishing family. Instead you’re a spendthrift man-child “living the dream”.

The funeral could be thought of as distilling everything that you hate about yourself. Everything that you must now murder. Put your foot on the neck of these things:

1. Scruffy appearance. You showed up without a suit. Underdressed to your Dad’s funeral.
2. Being a shit friend and family member. When Simon commented that the wedding was “last month’s news” he was right.
3. Amateurism. You didn’t check the piano was tuned, you didn’t rehearse enough with Biglad, you didn’t practice the trumpet piece enough. The performance values weren’t there.
4. Overstretching. You went for a piano piece that was too difficult to play under immense pressure: something simple would have done. You could have taken the intro off Sleepy Time, nailed the melody and defined a great cadenza. Instead you embarrassed yourself flailing away clumsily at an improvised chorus that never came.
5. Reticence. You didn’t sit with Mum in the service. You should have put yourself in the middle with the family and been there with your Mum. Instead you hid in the corner at the Piano.
6. Cowardice. You had an opportunity to tell the world how great your Dad was. Or at least read the eulogy. Oli stood up and spoke. You pussied out because nobody told you you had to talk.

Repeat after me:

1. I’m a scruffy, messy overgrown teenager.
2. I’m a crap friend and family member. Stuck in my own bubble.
3. I’m a total duffer professionally - I never really nail anything.
4. I’m delusional - constantly biting off more than I can chew rather than making steady progress.
5. I’m not really “in the room”. Just a lightweight who retreats to the edges.
6. I’m a coward - too scared of what people will think to commit to anything.

Learn from this. Dickhead. Harden up. Get into the 48 laws. Be a man.

=== 17 Junho.md ===

So back to the question: what would save live music? What saved it in Rio - street music, carnival, dressing up, debauchery. And a music tradition to hang it on. How can that be spread to other places?

What are the catalysts? Having cool repertoire there for adult and youth bands to play. Having people who have been to Rio Carnival and want to bring it back to their own city. Having blocos and brass bands in youth education programs. Permission to play in the street.

=== 17 March.md ===
# 17 March

2025

Reading *Brandraising 2.0 *and thinking about both your story and the story of Favela Brass. Ideally there would be a villain. Who/what is that? Certainly for you one answer is the rise of bland, electronic music (muzak) over live music and the unintended war against mastery waged by our electronic devices. The decline of popular music.

You found Brazilian music and thought it could be the live music to make that fightback, then you went there and it turned out to be the Brazilian spirit, Carnaval, brass bands, blocos, that has the power to defeat that enemy. Nothing compares to Carnaval.

The French music methods reinforce this war against dumbing down / attempt to reclaim mastery. Your piano practice is this. You’re trying to connect the kids to this old way of doing things. Also, the whole aim of getting 8 at grade 8 is a mastery goal.

One of the difficult things for you is that you don’t have much time for arranging - in a different time, you could dedicate yourself to it it, but now it’s something that you just about squeeze into a spare hour before work. You actually really want to be doing this kind of deep work, but you have the day job of running Favela Brass. 

Dick Hawdon, Eddie Harvey, Maestro Nelsinho, these were your guides.

But how does that villain manifest itself as on ongoing threatening presence during the film? Could the villain also be the logistical - the difficulty and cost of live music?

Taking it back to Star Wars, the enemy is the “Evil Empire”, with the Empire in some way representing the kind of faceless industrialization, in contrast to the Jedi’s more artisan abilities, notably the ability to use the force, and a light-saber. Is the evil empire Spotify, Taylor Swift, and Mark Zuckerberg - are these the forces of musical stagnation? Is it us vs the cellphone? 

The empire uses blasters, whereas the Jedi use light sabres. Music nowadays is made with software and plugins and recreated via JBLs, whereas our students are using real instruments.

Star Wars is a great way to frame the street brass band movement - a rebel alliance against crap electronic musak, and for music in the streets. 

2023

Great first rehearsal with Dan and Wesley. Really enjoyed the band being able to play without me. Also the collective impro lesson at the start went great - there’s a lot of momentum now. Stressed during the day though with all the admin crap - got to get this offloaded onto Pam and the team. Got to get out of the way.

It’s on the borderline between being easier to start from scratch. But it’s big, it’s exactly where you want to live and it has potential. It’s almost like you have to doublethink yourself that it was a house that you were given. Now make the most of it.

Thinking that in terms of the Favela Brass/arranging dilemma, the best thing may just be to go all in with the Anthony Trollope routine: 5:30 - 8:30 Monday to Friday with the first half of that being writing and the second half recording. Make that the big rock that the rest of the day is arranged around. Trollope wrote more than anyone else with that time, and you need to keep this away from weekends.

What Dad had yesterday turned out to be a severe stroke. His right arm is paralyzed and he can’t talk. Went back to the hospital on my own tonight and before I left, said goodbye and told him I loved him. He squeezed my hand.

I did think that this might be the moment to leave the favela. If you think about what he would have wanted, he would have wanted me safe and starting the family band with a beautiful black Brazilian girl. Can you make that happen in time?

=== 18 June-1.md ===
# 18 June

2022

Traveling back to Rio. Enjoying the journey listening to Paris, city of dreams, thinking about method stuff, planning, drinking wine and, yes, a cheeky coffee as well. Life is good.

Can’t help thinking about brass band music outside of Rio. Grandiose thoughts of helping groups all over the world bring people together in the streets - the whole live music vs Dj thing. You want to keep your feet on the ground but you also want to stretch in terms of impact.

What are you good at and what would have the most impact?

You’re good at writing arrangements, organizing learning materials and rehearsing bands - and playing all the instruments. Not so good as a long-term manager of people/relationships and also not got the killer business touch. 

Impact-wise it would be a bunch of music schools / bands all over the world copying Favela Brass, playing your arrangements basically. Maybe not setting up schools from scratch, but doing shorter courses at different places - running from couple of weeks to a term. Working with groups who already play a bit (remember that your strong point isn’t the beginner lessons - it’s the arrangements, the grooves, the impro teaching method.)

You want to get the movement for brass (and blocos) in the streets going. But on the musical side.

What is it that you have or do that is actually going to make such a difference?

=== 18 March.md ===
# 18 March

18 March

2022

2021

Went over the top again yesterday, this time went down via Vista Chinesa, Lagoa, Copacabana. Resolved to wrap up work-wise by 15:30 which meant that it wasn’t dark till I got to Copa - if I hadn’t had brake problems (luckily dropped on that bike shop/bar) I could have got further in the light. Back up at 19:40 so the whole thing must have lasted about 3 hours. Walked up Benjamin constant but rode the rest. Piano (Bach II original key) and trumpet practice (Bimbini duets) no problem on return.

At a particularly picturesque point, with the blood pumping through the legs, coming down towards the vista chinesa I had a bit of an epiphany: Rio is incredibly beautiful and you HAVE TO GET OUT IN THIS. The cycling is a very good start but you need to get out to the sea as well - a rowing club would be great, could also get down to the beach for volleyball, swim in the sea etc. After a jittery, cranky week, something like this really sorts you out.

When it’s 3 hours and with a good audio book (in this case “a world without email” by Cal Newport) you really zone in and move on from the daily troubles. Flow. This is so important - remember Andy Casterton and the cup of water? If you’re getting up at 5 (like today), you should be able to wrap up by 3:30, and if you haven’t got lessons or a meeting, getting out in nature and exercising is just the ticket.

Actually thought about trying a 3-hour batch of piano today to see how that goes - maybe longer stretches will get you into a deeper flow. But I think masses of exercise is the one for sorting your head out. You’re a border collie.

=== 19 December.md ===
# 19 December 

**2024**
**
**
The usual elements of the board are opposed to forwarding money from the main account to tide us over until we receive the cash from PRIO at the end of March. Had to listen to two hours of wisdom on the subject from Sômulo and Mirela last night. They want to drive the project off a cliff for fear of running out of petrol. 

You have been reacting too much recently. Saying too much. Not holding back. Not just at work but at home too. You’re not sleeping well and when you have a baby this will only get worse. You need a strategy to deal with this. To keep this stuff in you need to adopt a default silent front, a mask.

You did this in the meeting last night and it worked well. Just let them talk and talk and then make your point succinctly.

So it’s some kind of vow of silence - not a heavy, cold, un-smiling silence, but a definite and sustained commitment to holding things in. This has always been a problem for you. You need to be a bit more the Oracle at Delphi and a bit less Frank Spencer!
**

**2023**
**
**
LIstening to *SAS: Forged in Hell*, and haven’t been so into a book for a while. This is the right thing to be listening to in your situation. None of this talk of sabbaticals and handing over the reigns - just get on with it! The SAS combine imagination, courage, and hard training, which is essentially what floats your boat. Imaginação, coragem e duro treinamento.

**2020**

It’s a nice time this, hitting the big band arrangements in the morning, lots of nice food, tea and wine and watching good tv with the folks. By the end of Monday should have 3-4 recorded. Thinking about doing a lockdown video of me playing all instruments on Blinding Lights. Bit show offy but also a good bit of self promotion and will get people thinking about the band.

Joe Hewitt has been in touch about this possible grant from a cosmetics firm. Taking into account what he said I pitched the idea of trying to break the Guiness work record for the biggest ever melódica group at the end of next year. Current record is 688.

Main stumbling point is the price of the instruments but wouldn’t it be cool? 

Disadvantages:

If someone gave you £10k you wouldn’t buy 700 melódicas. It’s a very expensive publicity stunt.

You’ll have to do massive melódica classes at each school - will this work?

Joe wants his project to manage this project which could be a little tricky.

You don’t need 700 kids in the feeder program - you need 150. How are all these kids going to graduate on to horns?

If we involve private schools that could suck a lot of time and energy out of things like getting a big band ready for 2022.

Advantages:

Gives us a focus for 2021 and a success (hopefully) at the end of it.

It’s an easy thing to sell as a fundraising target (buy the instruments)

Schools will love being able to involve more kids

Possibly give us a nice little project to do with the private schools.

We will never need to buy melódicas again.

If Mangueirinha isn’t doing perc in the schools, we already need more melódicas / recorders.

Would get loads of media attention and lead on to other things. You could even do a Rouanet project just for this - 200.000k with most of that going on melódicas.

Could start partnership with hohner or Yamaha 

You’re entering into the mass arena which is really what Rio needs. Gives you and the project a higher profile.

It’s a story it’s a story it’s a story.

**2021**

End of year show at CIEP. The classic of classics of you stressing like crazy the night before and then it going ok. You couldn’t sleep, thinking about all the things that needed to be sorted, the board, Diane and Angelo, the logistics. Would have been good to make a diary of all that.

Having moved the event to CIEP because of possible rain of course on the day we got blazing sunshine. But I think CIEP was better - somewhere different for the end of year event. Putting the kids on the banked seating worked, and Camila’s video turned out an absolute peach.

Diane clearly loved it and now wants us to play on an oil rig! 🤷‍♂️ Need to thank Angelo properly. Do you remember Sômulo reading through your set list and notes? Nutter. Next time just print out the lyrics to “tristeza” and leave it on the stand. And then Bindu ringing up the next day to “debrief” you and try and micromanage the communications 🤮.

=== 19 September.md ===
# 19 September

19 September

2024

In the rhythm of 25-30 mins piano in the morning (with coffee). It is so enjoyable and with the element of zero tolerance of errors becomes an exercise in concentration. At the king’s coronation a calligrapher was tasked did the lettering on the record by hand without mistakes. This is the kind of human feat that you admire and it feels great to walk the tightrope of playing a tune in a different key by memory and get to the end without mistakes. It’s time out of the day, but it gets you out of bed, it gets you concentrating, it expands you musically and most all you enjoy it intensely. This is your ritual, your times crossword.

2020

Missed the diary yesterday this really does need to be done first thing. Also missed the piano - should also be first thing.

Been working on this Natura grant with Carola and, surprisingly, it hasn’t been ideal. She wrote some parts well but in other parts missed the main important points to get in, and at other points downright sloppy. The real problem is when you try to get her to change stuff she digs her heels in, or does things like just copying in the bullet points of the points I sent, rather than putting them in text. Very long, impenetrable paragraphs. Ended up telling her that me and Joe would do the last revision. Joe wants to do our grant-writing and has done a revision already. If he’s good at it, I don’t have a problem with that. 

Finally got the meeting with the accountant, Sr. Milton. Went fine and cleared up most stuff. We’re better off with a UK account otherwise it’s complicated to spend pounds. Angelo didn’t set up the board meeting, even after the chat.

Spending quite a lot of time on the Favela Brass Keynote presentation. This stuff is important.

=== 19th November.md ===
# 19th November

19th November

2020

Quite lethargic at this moment. Been dialing caffeine, booze and food back so not overly surprised. Didn’t quite get as stuck into the finances I would like today, but the arranging is going well. Looking back at past diaries I can’t help wondering how much better off I would be if, instead of going round in circles thinking about MLT, I had just worked on arranging for the 1st 90 mins of the working day.

2019

I now have a working computer, printer and internet connection. Life is good. Hopefully now I’ll be able to get on top of things. At the moment the focus is not on the curriculum so much as the organisation of the project - produção. The general idea is to set things up so you have systems and checklists on Google drive that other people can use.

This is especially important because your memory is not the greatest. Get it all down on paper/spreadsheets. Do the role, set up a system and pass it on.

Ind the end, what do you want to be doing? I think overseeing the system is the way forward. Giving some lessons to test materials, and being an ambassador for the project. The position of Executive Director makes sense because that allows you to get paid.

Ideally, you would be executive director, then hand that off to someone else (Joe?) and be president of the board. Then hand that off as well and do something else but stay as advisor, maybe volunteer Musical Director (or paid musical director!) Maybe longer term looking at wider music service in Rio

[2020 comment - the idea of becoming a volunteer Musical Director in the end shows how you need to look out for yourself more. Obviously after all this if you’re still working for Favela Brass you, above all people, should be getting paid]

=== 2 April.md ===
# 2 April

2024

2022

Alice’s birthday. Didn’t get her a pressy but bought Amazon voucher. Did the cake and happy birthday over Zoom. Printed out the John MacAllister warm-ups - you don’t have to do this all yourself. 

Spending the afternoon drinking a very nice bottle of Portuguese wine and listening to music. Have to say this is one of my favorite things to do. Spotify is great now with the radio option.

Certain tracks take you straight back to your teens. With that come strong saudades for Dad. At least now the end is a bit less prevalent and you can focus more on just missing him. Dreamt quite vividly last night that he was still alive, not for the first time. Was a pleasant dream though. 

Read somewhere about someone making a death bed promise to their father. Don’t forget that you did this. The band of brown grandkids. Do it for dad, and Mum, do it for them, and your future wife, and for yourself. Don’t sleep on this. You made a promise.

What you really want is to listen to and make great music with friends. Why not do a curry every so often? Much better than what you were doing taking hotel rooms alone. When you have leisure time you yearn to be with other people. That’s curry clube and this thing in Lapa.

Mate, you’re 42, live a little. Find a recorder teacher for the schools. Favela brass is better with you bringing the network together and doing the music part. Get your amp back, do a curry and then work out how to get other people involved. I reckon Friday is good. Don’t worry about a band straight off.

If we’re talking about spirituality and all that crap, having a drink and listening to great music with friends is absolutely fundamental for you. Once a week. You’ve been struggling with this leisure thing for a bit. Invite people over for a curry, have a jam at cozinha da Lapa and you’re good.

Later…

The thing about Dad was that he was solid. He held his own. He didn’t fawn, didn’t lose his dignity. Ever. Witty, sharp. Never played the fool. He was a proper father with strong limits. You are your own man, but don’t give yourself away. Hold your end up, hold the family end up. Find a way to honour your Dad. 

Really, when you think about it, Dad’s funeral was a testament to your pettiness. You should have given him the New Orleans burial. You just didn’t want to get Stugger involved. Fool.

Ah, and don’t forget to do this. Have a drink, put the headphones on and listen to great music. This is your holiday.
This is how to put it all in perspective.

When you drink you think: drop it. Get back in touch with Stugger, with the boys, get together for a beer and listen to some music. Drop it with Fernando Pereira. Go to Stugger’s wedding. Be loyal. Drop it with Marcia, Somulo, Bindu. Fucking DROP IT! Live and let live. Chill the fuck out!

I don’t know what the hangover will be like tomorrow but I think this is worth it. Connect with yourself, with what’s important. Music.

Carnaval got me thinking:

1. kitfanfarra.com with links to arrangeme.com would be a great contribution. Brazilians will pirate it all anyway, but it won’t be your fault. Think of all the clips with 
. Could do flexible instrumentation (voice 1 = Tpt/Alto/sop etc.) - remember the problem with brassify is who will play the charts?
2. If you’re in the live music experience business there is nowhere on earth like this. Don’t carp on about how cariocas are untrustworthy/unprofessional - just think about how perfect this place is for brass band music. Best audiences ever.
3. Getting (good) foreign brass bands here would be a worthy mission: do a sponsored festival to get them paid, then let them loose in the streets like NYBB.
4. Having your own brass band would be amazing. Especially come carnival time. Don’t let another carnival go by without your arrangements in effect.

Came back home and made arrangement of “voce partiu meu coração” whilst sipping whisky. Fantastic.

=== 20 June.md ===
# 20 June

2023
By coincidence you just watched a Robert Greene video about consistency over passion and were just about to write that you need to commit to doing 1 pom of piano and 3 poms of brass band arranging first thing. That and the daily dozen études on trumpet gives you the « holy trinity ».

Point is that there are lots of other great immersive work projects that you should also spend time on: teaching materials, planning, recording arrangements, training video etc. So you can’t really commit to 3 hours of just arranging, but 3 pomodoros you can do and you can do almost all days. 1 more pomodoro practicing sax would be magic but at the moment it would be a bridge too far.

Last year you were looking for the name, and it eventually came: Brassify - an absolute corker. And now you’re not going to use it?

BNDES show goes well. President wants to talk to Sômulo about projects. Working on Ed Sheehan shape of you arrangement. Commit to doing 1 pom of piano and 3 poms of brass band arranging first thing, even if you have to have a cup of tea. Still off on one thinking of names for your brass site: street brass omnibook?

=== 23 Jan.md ===
# 23 Jan

DAILY NUGGET - THE INFJ

Two personality tests have put you down as an INFJ - the rarest personality type for a man. More specifically an INFJ-A - or the Assertive Advocate (assertive as opposed to turbulent advocate ). I mean, it’s all one step off a horoscope, but it’s food for thought as well. Here’s the career bit:

*Advocates’ needs may be hard to meet in some work environments, especially those that offer little independence and agency. Advocate personalities are sometimes drawn to behind-the-scenes and noncompetitive roles, but these jobs can lead to frustration if they don’t allow Advocates to act as they see fit, grow as individuals, and make a difference.*
*
*
*For this reason, people with the Advocate personality type may feel fulfilled by seeking out leadership positions or by starting their own business. By finding jobs that offer more autonomy, Advocates can focus on applying their creativity and integrity to everything they do. Advocates may also find it gratifying to create bridges between seemingly disparate professional fields – for example, by writing about psychology or by being an environmental lawyer. These hybrid careers can offer plenty of opportunities for Advocates to exercise their creativity and their love of learning.*
*
*
*Where Advocates struggle is in work that doesn’t take personal needs into consideration, is overly repetitious, or promotes conflict. Jobs with these characteristics can leave Advocates frustrated and unfulfilled. People with this personality type may also chafe at the criticism and pressure that come with cutthroat, competitive work environments.*
***## 
***
*In truth, Advocate personalities can do well in any field. To be truly happy, however, they need to find work that aligns with their values and allows them some independence. Advocates crave opportunities to learn and grow alongside the people they are helping. When this happens, Advocates may finally feel as if they are fulfilling their life’s mission, contributing to the well-being of humanity on a personal level.*

[If only personalities were that simple…]

2025

Building work on the upstairs of the house in its early stages, but seems to be going ok. Fábio already making noises that it might run over time - he’s saying 3 months now, which would mean mid-April. That’s right on the line baby-wise.

Productive if not particularly long day’s work - managed to carve out an hour at the start to write music (trying to do something with Stanton Warriors “The Antidote” as a starting point). Rob Fletcher is going for it with the databases. Starting to think that we have to limit the numbers in the lessons in the favela now. With a 15% attrition rate, you need 121 in the project and 25 coming in each year. That’s plenty. Big is vulnerable - and the noises coming from Ivan and the sisters about the Assunção aren’t encouraging.

10 years video project difficult going in-between Taylor and Maria. Camila being extremely annoying as usual and not doing her part as well. Not one I’d hire again. Having said that I think the video will turn out well. Fingers crossed…

Nice online meeting with Rolf from the Biquinis de Ogodó - looks like we’re on for Cacilda in Ilha Grande.

Yesterday the dog known as Catinga got her paws run over as she was running alongside you and Zola. Was looking very much like you and Thamires would take her to the vet and then adopt, but Priscila who lives next to the padaria took her in. Lovely dog but it would be a bold step given that you have a baby on the way and a 6-week trip to the UK planned. Tricky.

Then today you and Zola were bitten by the psycho dog on the road down to Ancestral. You could have handled it all a bit better, but then again you’re human. What was worse though was coming home to Thamires who was too preoccupied with chewing you out for leaving the front door open (again), to show any interest whatsoever in the fact that you just got bitten. She just chewed you about what you said or didn’t say to the owners. 

You have to take some responsibility here - you could do a lot better around the house, and you’re not shagging her enough. But Christ almighty I hope this is a phase, because the baby isn’t even born yet and there is a very long, difficult road ahead.

# 24 Jan

2023

Last night had the whole indecision and self-flagellation thing about the interview process. Just the most horrible feeling - calling yourself an incompetant indecisive eedjut who shouldn’t be allowed to go out of the house, let alone run and NGO. Then sorted it out in the morning. Dude, don’t forget the negative capability thing. Whether it’s what Keats meant or not, you have to be able to tolerate that things might not go right, or you might look a twat, or your might upset someone. You have to be able to tolerate the not knowing, the sense that maybe you’re screwing it all up, being a dick, making a fool of yourself without pulling the plug. If you’re going to make stuff you have to be able to deal with risk, imperfection, things maybe not working out and take it all with a pinch of salt and god forbid a sense of humour. It’s either that or going and living in a cave.

Ah and another thing: stop being so frikking creepy. Just think about what creepy people do and don’t do that.

Watched *All Quiet on the Western Front. *Good for putting things in perspective.

2022

The other thing is that you seem like a bona fide hsp (highly sensitive person). Both diagnoses are helpful. You need to do less, avoid management roles, stick to the creative stuff. Cut down (or out) the caffeine and booze, exercise loads, and meditate. And spend lots of time at the piano.

**2021**

Somulos BNDES thing - bit boring and embarrassing you not remembering all the monthly donors. But positive - this is a move in the right direction. You have a good board team work on getting a good vibe going.

Had the idea of polos for Favela Brass. You have one in Santa (AP1) and one in Flamengo (AP2), each with schools flowing in - don’t try and get all the kids together at once. Do one oficina central at Flamengo and the other in Santa. Keeps numbers in each oficina manageable.

You have the Assunção - use it! Get into the schools that feed into it. Only thing is the whole drugs traffic thing. You would be raising the local profile again when you were kind of looking to sidestep all that.

Think... one oficina is let’s say one teacher each for trom, sax, tpt and Perc. Plus one horn and one perc for main rehearsal, and you for other bit. 7 profs, R$1.260 a week 60.000 a year. Each school is 2 profs and you need 3 feeder schools for an oficina. So that’s another 1.080 a week gives about 100k a year per polo in teachers, with capacity at 96 at central oficina and 72 in perc/recorder lessons. R$60 a student just teacher costs.

2 polos gives room for private students - CEAT for Santa. Liceu for Flamengo. Also eliminates transport costs. Think: would the students in Santa really go to Flamengo every week?

=== 24 March.md ===
# 24 March

2025

Still thinking about this idea of you being the guide in the whole Favela Brass story, rather than the hero. It makes sense on a lot of levels:

- It means you don’t want to play in Cacilda in the end - you want them to take it and run with it

- Your lesson is all about teaching students how to “use the force”, rather than just being musical robots

- It means your own doubts and struggles aren’t the focus - you can just be the competent, down-to-earth coach that in reality is what is needed from you

- Even with the admin side of Favela Brass, there’s a lot of power in you adopting the posture of someone helping the team and board to move solve their problems themselves rather than being the big leader

- It unties you from the day to day of Favela Brass long term - Rio had this problem, you were on hand to show them the way to sort it, and then they take it and run with it.

=== 25 August.md ===
# 25 August

25 August

2022

British school in morning ostensibly to check what sound equipment is at the Botafogo site for the BCS, but Zezo had hidden agenda of trying to rope me into a class 5 band program at barra. It’s a temptation.
