2020

Woken in the night by a call from David Merrylees from the BCS which buggered up my sleep. But straight after the call did have a slurry of breakthroughs in terms of MLT thoughts. 

Have been practicing pieces around the keys on the piano and when I went to have a noodle on the piano at home yesterday, things started opening up in terms of modulating between keys. Only in the middle of the night did I realise that a lot of the modulation that was now coming naturally was the middle section of the Bach piece that I had been studying.

Started to think in terms of a wire mesh that represents what you can “hear” - maybe the auditory cortex. Sitting at the piano, determined by all I have listened to before, things that I want to play pop up, but they only get played if I can “reach for them”. Almost like proprioception - you can sense where you want to move your arm to - but can you make it go there?

The ability to play something that you hear is tied more to mechanical movement. It’s direct. The key question is: have I done something like this before? How many times? Learning through feedback is absolutely relevant here and the theory comes in more as a way to calculate how to find things you want to practice, and contextualize that which you already know, rather than to achieve direct proficiency. 

Once things start getting hairy, theory becomes less and less useful in the task of comprehending the link between the sound and the instrument. This starts to become apparent when modulations come in, but also points to the limitations of the chord/scale approach to jazz improvisation. These relationships need to be “felt” and “seen”. The powerhouse of all of this is visuo-spatial to auditory learning. The theory is like an overlay, a ruler, and you will never play a game of football well if you  have to measure each step with a ruler first - it is posterior learning that acts as a scaffold for future study.

That is not to denigrate theory entirely. There is the kind of gestalt understanding which doesn’t have a visual or spatial form, the “ghost” that transfers between keys. Theoretical understanding aids this sense of context. Knowing what something is not only by where it is on the instrument, but also by theory. 

A way of theorize this might be thinking in terms of different aspects of performing a given motif. You have the wire-mesh, where you can hear the idea that you want to reach for, you have the flesh and blood, physical connection where you can reach for it on the instrument, and you have ruler of theory, where you can pull up a conscious understanding of what is going on when needed. These three things feed the ghost of gestalt understanding and creativity.

Reading about the neuroscience of music has helped here - auditory cortex, motor areas, visual cortex, gestalt understanding and also the limbic system, emotional circuits all coming together. Back to Amersterdam, the more that fires, the stronger the emergent understanding. Just like consciousness, the ghost of musical understanding arises from the connections between all of these areas.

When I pick up a new instrument the theory, the auditory signal and the gestalt understanding are there. Even the visuospatial in there in the form of the piano representation running in the background. All that is needed is time playing, to create the direct connections to the specific movements of this instruments to the gestalt.

Just look up “gestalt psychology” and read the phrase “The whole is other than the sum of its parts” - Kurt Koffka. Never was that more true than in learning music - it links directly to Amsterdam. The ghost emerges. Also “Gestalt principles are in the mind, not the eye”. Just like how ear training is in the brain and nervous system, not the ear. And “Gestalt psychology is the examination of our senses versus perception.”

Another thing to think about is the observation that the chess masters distinguish themselves from mere mortals almost exclusively on the amount of plays that they are familiar with. And what is the mechanism for harmonic progressions to become “familiar” to the musician? They need to go through all the keys (preferably on the piano), with theoretical understanding. Theory creates almost like a second window, a programming consul, with a technical read-out of what’s going on the music - a different way of perceiving it which feeds the gestalt.

The senses is the “muscle-memory” of playing a specific motif on an instrument, whereas the perception is the gestalt understanding of music. Also think in terms of “anticipatory headroom” - the chess master can anticipate the impending options, and in music, especially harmony it’s a similar thing. Remember how when you’re improvising you often predict your next “stock” phrase and then give it a twist? You understand the expections, working with, and against them. Chess.

This is good:

_http://rebirthofreason.com/Articles/Maurone/Beyond_Emotion_The_Gestalt_Theory_of_Music.shtml__
_
_
_
“In musical situations where people do not have expectancies…the music will be meaningless for them.

“So far as music is concerned, the argument from here…when people here a sequence of tones, they group these into perceptual units which will be as ‘good as the prevailing conditions allow.’ Assuming that they can do this with some success, the sequence of tones will become meaningful, and will be a ‘tune’ in the sense in which we have previously defined tunes.”

Davies continues: “This tendency to organic separate units into some sort of whole is one of the central tenets of Gestalt psychology. Kurt Koffka…one of the pioneers of the Gestalt approach to perception, further postulated the ‘law of Pragmanz,’ or ‘law of the best figure’: According to this, there is a natural tendency for observers to prefer the simplest and most stable figure available to them; unfortunately he does not offer an explanation for the terms ‘simple’ or ‘stable’. Applying the law of Pragnanz to the Gestalt theory, Koffka reasoned that ‘The psychological organization will always be as good as the prevailing conditions allow. The act of perception therefore seeks to impose the best and most stable organization possible upon the percepts available…”.
 
The law of Pragmanz predicts why movable Do on an instrument doesn’t work - we’re trying to force children to think in terms of a more complex system than that which is presented to them physically. Whatever you do has to be at least grounded in the more simple physical figure that is presented to them - I.e. the fixed notes of the instrument.

“When music goes out of its way to violate the very expectations that it sets up, we call it ‘expressive.’ Musicians breathe ‘feeling’ into a piece by introducing minute deviations in timing and loudness. And composers build expression into their compositions by PURPOSELY [emphasis mine] violating anticipations that have been established.”

“Jourdain rounds out the theory with a kinesthetic idea of musculature representation: “…if music does not channel directly to our muscles, then we must consciously put it there. It seems that we use our musculatures to represent music, modeling the most important features of musical patterns by means of physical movements large and small. At one extreme, we bounce up and down to a pulsing beat. At the other, we are immobile yet are racked by anticipations of movement, experiencing the impetus toward motions that we do not actually initiate.” He cautions us, however, that “this view is necessarily speculative, since there is no science of muscular representation. For that matter, there is no hard-and-fast typology of physical movements or of musical devices by which we could compare sonic and somatic experience…yet it is easy to imagine two functions, that such representations would serve. First, representation provides a sort of notation system in which we momentarily inscribe features of music as it passes by, and thereby more easily remember those features over many seconds… A second function of muscular representation is to amplify our experience of music. Musical patterns that produce emotion and pleasure are replicated in a second, particularly extensive neural system-the motor system-and so emotion and pleasure arise in this second medium as well as in the direct experience of sound.” In essence, “…we use our bodies as resonators for auditory experiences.””

Right, that’s quite enough of that.

Cafe Nero at noon today to see Stugger and Carola. Here goes…

Spent the morning thinking about the organization of the lessons and it did pay off - had the idea to put mangueirinha in the schools plus you and volunteers doing recorder and the fundamentals/melódica course on same day. You can open or close the tap in terms of how many new students you accept each term. Tailor to each school - basically just do your best for each group (some may even turn into school bands).

Nice idea of the individual schools being like rivers leading into the bay (of Guanabara). Also, coringa would be a good name for a music method.

Had a thought. What you’re doing is sorting out music Ed in Brazil. Not by imposing a big system, but by finding a formula that works here - the schools and social projects flowing into the oficina. The bloco, the percussion, the big band and especially the grade system. That is really something that could scale. Just listing tunes and keys for each grade would bypass copyright.

Doesn’t the name coringa fit in with this? The coringa can be played at any time, it stands for flexibility, adaptability, universality. The musical fundamentals are the same across genres, so the coringa can fit in whatever the music project. Tunes in any style can be graded. By inviting Brazil to use a grading system you are almost playing a wild card that seems like it’s nothing, but could have big consequences.

=== 26th December.md ===
# 26th December 

DAILY NUGGET

**Go for the prestige strategy over the dominance strategy.**

This comes from Will Stoor’s AOM interview about his book The Status Game. The idea is that the general tendency is to default too much to the dominance strategy when challenged, trying to establish your superior status to the person in that situation. If, however, you try to find opportunities to give other people status and prestige wherever possible, you will find that status flowing back to you. 

*“. . . we all too easily slip into dominance, and you know, these little acts of dominance that mark our days you know, when we kind of roll our eyes, send rude emails when we feel that we’ve been slighted. And it’s a much better strategy, I think, to try and use these small moments of prestige, try to make people feel good as much as possible, even though in the short term we might not get our way. Because people love status, if you get a reputation as somebody that is generous with your status, and makes people feel good about themselves, people are gonna wanna be with you, and you’re gonna get lots of status coming back your way. So I think it’s very easy, and it’s in our kind of animal nature, our pre-human nature, to push back with dominance all the time. But I think to mindfully go to prestige is a really useful thing."*

2022

Oli’s clan still over. Walk, games, mulled wine etc. Still up on the air about PRIO deposits. 

2021

Belém with Mum, Val and Hardy. The monastery was inspiring, the weather less so. Missed the offer on the MacBook Air in FNAC. Nice restaurant meal later on at the place that did Portuguese-style cachaça but got hit with a 222 euro bill. Drank a lot - will be feeling that today no doubt.

2020 - COVID Christmas with Mum and Dad. I was on barbecue duty doing the pigs in blankets and chipolatas. I finished up on Christmas Eve at 5pm then hid from the phone for 24 hours. Highly recommended - need to get this thing in check, have slots for checking the phone then put it out of reach. Nice game of slightly drunk scrabble in the evening which Dad won.

Finished The Weeknd Blinding Lights arrangement and vídeo today. Pretty happy all told. Video is a bit indulgent I guess but I do think you have to be realistic: writing big band arrangements for some future hypothetical band is not the same thing as writing them so you can make a YouTube vid where it will get listened to and seen.

These arrangements are a thing unto themselves: whatever happens at Favela Brass they are their own achievement and a concrete contribution to the cause. If you keep pumping them out good things will come of this. For a start, it’s a musical mission statement: this is where we want Favela Brass to get to. They also open the door to exchanges and are an excellent calling card for yours truly.

Let these arrangements be your artistic escape from the draining politics of being director of favela brass. This and the piano is your “you” time. Pay yourself first. 

Have been running in the mornings which is the key to feeling human.

2021

Had a cracking week. 4 good tweaks:

1. Fasting from lunchtime to breakfast on weekdays
2. Getting up bang on 5 and cycling every morning
3. Having a coffee and doing a 90-min deep work session on the syllabus first thing.
4. Moving the meeze and main trumpet practice to after 5pm

Fasting has contributed to better sleep and weight loss. Getting up at 5 has also helped on the sleep front (and productivity). The 90-min morning deep work means that every day, no matter how bogged down you get with admin, you can look back and know that the course has improved - you made a deposit in the savings account. The meeze and trumpet in the evening is great because the morning time is exchanged for deep work time and you spend the evening in “cleaning mode”, getting the next day organized so you can relax.

Really not fun. Alternate sparkling water with beer so you at least avoid the beginnings of a hangover.

The first lesson is not to shit where you eat. Ever. The other is to work on the PE and move your network forward. Find the silver lining. Onwards and upwards. What good could come of this? 

=== 27 Jan 2022.md ===
# 27 Jan 2022

27 Jan 2022

DAILY NUGGET - Mastery

You long to create your niche. To find the little thing that you excel at, and are continually honing. The idea of being a back-office boffin, who just potters around in his cave inventing creative gismos that help everyone else - the code-breaker. One danger in this is that you end up presiding over a crazy, ever-changing method that doesn’t get used - just as you presided over a crazy ever-changing set of big band arrangements that didn’t get used. The other danger is that you end up in a position that doesn’t suit your nature - spending the whole time dealing with people, power politics, harsh criticism, management, meetings and a crushing volume of administrative details all at the same time.

How to carve that niche? 

Same role within Favela Brass: For this you would have to delegate everything non-music related. Have staff that handle pretty much everything except the music side. You just make sure everyone is paid, keep the board happy and take the first few hours of the day to work on the method. This requires you finding good staff. 

Another role within Favela Brass: For this you would need to point Favela Brass in the right direction, get the board on the same page, put in an Executive Director who won’t go off the tracks (Cris?), and then put yourself in a position where they can’t do without you. Diretor Artístico/Pedagógico. It’s risky because the others could make decisions that make you want to leave.

Outside Favela Brass: For this you would want to point FB in the right direction then get out completely. Take your CV elsewhere, or set your own little self-employed business up. You could do a lucrative school for rich students, adult students, our your could find some way to sell your method books.

*"Your skill level will reach a point where you will be able to claim your independence from within the group you work for and move out on your own. In a world in which there is so much we cannot control, this will bring you the ultimate form of power. You will determine your circumstances. As your own Master, you will no longer be subject to the whims of tyrannical bosses or scheming peers.”*
*
*
- *Robert Greene*

2022

Yesterday was a bit of a write-off. So much to do but just couldn’t think. Did eventually manage to define the lessons in Pereira which was the most difficult bit. Really do hate having so many things on the radar at once. Looked at house prices in Santa Teresa - if you got somewhere with a spare room or two for Airbnb it could be a good investment. Went to Mustafa’s to record trombone then realized I wasn’t going to get anywhere near it. Stressed at the moment, not the worst time, but not the best. Just feels like it’s all piling up. Had that dream where Dad was with us, you tried to take a photo and then woke up.


=== 27 Jan.md ===
# 27 Jan

27 Jan

2025

Watched the film “Living” last night, about an old bureaucrat in London in the 1950s who discovers he has cancer and decides to start living his life more.

As he reflects on his life, the main character says that all he wanted to be was a gentleman when he was younger. To be one of those men in suits and bowler hats that got on the train to London and made the crust for their family. That was the model of your Dad’s generation, and it was his model for you. You’re now both more and less than that, but the point is that if you’re looking at a reference for how to live your life, how to be the kind of person that you admire, then you already have a reference from inside your own culture. The book “Infantalized” describes how this vision has died and now everyone learns they should follow their dream and let it all hang out.

You’re going to going to be a father in 3 months’ time. If ever there was a time to grow up, this is it. You’re never going to be Marcus Aurelius, but maybe you could work a bit more on being a gentleman in the day-to-day?

Isn’t there also a paradox in trying to be a gentleman, like there is a paradox in trying to be happy? Happiness isn’t found in trying to be happy: it is found in living well. Similarly, if your objective is for you, personally, to be the perfect gentleman, then maybe you’ll miss the overall point, which is about how you treat other people. Isn’t that also the essence of growing up - shifting the focus away from me me me?

I was pretty destroyed energy-wise this evening and I still think some kind of drinking vow is coming on. Just read that “binge drinking in midlife is associated with increased risk of dementia.” Binge drinkers being defined as people who drink more than the equivalent of a bottle of wine in one sitting once a month. Your body will go on and on, it’s the brain you should worry about.

ICMS is very behind which makes it unlikely we’ll have it in time for Petrobras. You’re not having a holiday from Favela Brass that’s for certain. It just doesn’t stop.

Reputation is everything and if you’re working with kids part of the reputation needs to be that you are highly responsible. The think you need to keep front and center is that one slip can ruin years of good work.

You may find you have your work cut out now. But we are where we are so what can be done now?

Not drinking is a possibility. Maybe try a break up to the next Carnaval. A reputation for being teetotal will help you, as will the extra time and energy.

Long term, living outside the favela could help. Less gossip.

=== 28 March.md ===
# 28 March

28 March

2021

“Success is not final; failure is not fatal: it is the courage to continue that counts”
- Churchill

Borgen can always be relied on for a good quote. Very glad that I’m rationing these episodes to one a week - don’t want it to end. Can’t put my finger on why I enjoy it so much.

How can I sum up the present moment? Worried about COVID, about getting and spreading it - Brazil is starting to really lose control and 6% of deaths with the new variant are younger than you. Went for a pizza at Hedi’s on Saturday and you and Joe both regretted it. That’s off the menu now (pardon the pun). Lessons are suspended at the convent and the aterro and I’m not in any hurry to start back. It’s more serious now.

Today is Sunday but turned it into a Deep Work day. Just had a week on Green Tea only which was a little on the unproductive side, but really helped to recharge the batteries. Had a jar of black tea today and I was off - finished the first “Technical Comprehension” book today and very proud of it. Really excited that it hits the harder to reach fundamentals of musical understanding in a way that other music teachers can fairly easily teach. No two-week training courses or any of that rubbish.

I like the idea of reversing the dynamic: rather than trying to have weekends off coffee, why not have just weekends on coffee? That way you don’t get addicted. Just have to deal with a caffeine hangover rather than caffeine withdrawal and while you are doing that you have two full days of solid Deep Work to look forward to. Two (or even one) caffeinated deep work days would be awesome and you could spend the rest of the time pottering knowing the DW will get done. Less switching.

That said, on green tea last week I solved a lot of big-picture problems. Had the fitas de Bomfim idea, worked out the structure for the lessons when we go back, etc. It’s like a lens - if you want to zoom out, green tea and little caffeine, if you want to zoom in, black tea/coffee (black tea is fine).

Date with Luana Friday (aterro do Flamengo). Great girl, unfortunately her having 3 kids limits it a bit.

At the board meeting last week they were busy congratulating themselves on the great finances last year. But the reality is that sound finances for the project were paid for out of your finances. Where’s this going? At some point, you have to land this plane.

Looking at the above at 1 in the morning after a bunch of whisky, I can’t help thinking it all sounds just a bit petty and boring.

# 28 November

2022

Stressful week. Had the whole thing about the board voting on the FOCA project issue, but not just that. Maria Rita’s mum and Geiza being dicks and saying their kids won’t go on trips because they can’t go. And now Cris getting upset at my criticisms of her at the Blues Festival.

What to do? I guess get the caffeine down - at least switch to tea. You’re stressed, feeling like you just need to be unwired for a bit. That’s coffee (as well as circumstances). You need that even keel, that extra bit of self control in the tank before saying something hurtful. We need good Tom back.

You know the drill, loads of exercise, meditate every day, no booze or caffeine, don’t overeat.

=== 28 October-1.md ===
# 28 October 


=== 28 October.md ===
# 28 October

28 October

2022

Board meeting last night which had very little in the way of discussion. We’re gearing up for the strategy meeting on Saturday. After showing signs of reasonableness Bindu started questioning whether I have the right skillset for musical director or whether we shouldn’t get someone else. One of the big risks here is that Bindu and Sômulo start trying to bulldoze the new Executive Director. Need more directors, make that list now.

In terms of mission, I’m thinking that as I leave I could point to 3 things that would make an activity not Favela Brass:

1. WHAT. Departing from Brass Band and Bloco set-up and our mix of pop, MPB and jazz/second line (or giving in to people asking us to teach other things).

Why? The project is intended to put kids from lower incomes at the head of this whole brass band movement thing. It’s not just about music, it’s about popular brass band street music - the music that has a chance of keeping live music as part of popular music culture.

1. WHO. Giving lessons to rich kids as defined as private school, or to adults.

Why? We won’t solve the problem of an elite Carnaval by teaching rich kids. If they pay it’s worse because the demanding parents will pull the focus away from the favela kids. A project for rich kids or adults raising money for Favela Brass would be great, but let them organize that with the benefit of their own cash and connections.

1. WHERE. Managing projects outside Rio de Janeiro.

Why? Rio de Janeiro is the most important place in the world for live music but poorer kids don’t get a look in. Rio is the place where the street band culture and grass roots education gap is extreme - that is the problem we are trying to fix. Operationally, all of RJ state is a bus ride which makes for much stronger exchange possibilities. Without RJ state we lose these possibilities. Train partner projects around the world like Fight for Peace, but don’t actively manage them. Loose franchise. Friends of Favela Brass.

1. HOW. Abandoning grade system and long term approach. 1-year projects without evaluation.

Why? The project is about excellence. Not just poor kids learning music, but poor kids raising the bar in Rio de Janeiro. It’s a local authority music service, not a social project.

Told Cris I’m moving over and she said “I’m yours - do with me what you will!”. We could do a lot worse than sticking her in as DE.

2021

Curitiba. Went to the wrong airport. R$1100 down the drain. Dorcas was kind of depressing - these social projects are such a band aid. Did your coloured scale reference with the kids which was the wrong thing to do, but it’s a great tool and a great way to learn music.

Had the idea on the plane to do grades just based on scales and rhythm reading. As your Dad said - HOLD THAT THOUGHT! 

Afternoon tea with Ragnilde and her dinosaur eggs and beers at Tio Ali’s house - really good guy, enjoyed the chat about Brazilian music. Ed’s a great guy and can teach you a lot. Exchange trip off though as he’s in Trancoso Jan, things have soured with the Antonina núcleo, the hotel isn’t available off peak, and Curitiba in geral isn’t that impressive for the kids.

2020

What started out pretty inauspiciously turned into quite a productive day. Notching down from black to green tea at the moment and shortly after starting work arranging lindo lago de amor I just hit a wall of fatigue and ended up lying down. Did end up finishing the arrangement, but late.

Then just hit the bitty admin stuff, including starting the process moving for us having exams in January, completing old MEI declarations and later paying MEI payments down at the bank. Did recording for Luiz Henrique and was nice to put a little money in my pocket.

Finished the making of a chef which was a better book than I thought it would be and held your attention very well for some reason. Now moved on to devil in the kitchen which is promising to be even better.

2019

Busy weekend with the kids. Saturday morning music centre at CIEP went very well. Only 12 kids for 5 teachers but it went really well and CIEP let us uses the quadra 8am - 12am. Cacilda rehearsal afterwards went well and the whole format seemed to make a lot of sense. Now we need to think about how to get Favela Brass kids there (from the favelas).

Shows at Largo do Machado and Fluminense football club went well as well. Maria Rita and Maria Fernanda absent as well as Samuel Ribeiro. Felt a bit light numbers-wise.

Spent Sunday morning putting together shared GTD lists for me Carola & Joe. Realizing that Carola wasn’t doing much of the stuff that production should be helping with - communicating with parents, posting on Facebook/Instagram, helping at shows, editing videos. Instead you’re doing a lot of the production stuff while she defines the project.

The challenge now is to find time for your tasks both as Musical and Executive Director. Wouldn’t it be nice not to have to do Tuesdays and Thursdays at TBS?

All the sticky decisions, difficult people. Not wanting to turn in tonight and bring the weekend to an end. Just do your best, do your job, make the best decisions that you can. Then get on to the music side of things at FB - let someone else take the heat who thrives off that kind of thing.

About last year’s diary. Yes it’s the antagonism, maybe more specifically demeaning other people - not necessarily getting all up in other people’s faces, but just not giving them proper respect. According to the BEST model in *Hire with you Head *that’s the danger with technicians and it rings true for you.

2022

DAILY NUGGET - Your antagonism = Their disloyalty

The one trait that will give you the most trouble is you antagonism. Popularity is power. Think of it like a network - a person who is on your side is a green node, a person who isn’t is a red node. Every short-tempered interaction invites a red node. Every time you slag someone off and they find out about it you’re creating a contagious red node. People want to be around people who are creating green nodes for them, and will try to create other red nodes for their own red nodes. Compound interest. See the Antagonism x Loyalty spreadsheet, and BE NICE TO PEOPLE.

Ah, and here’s the key thing: you don’t have to be being antagonistic toward the person in question to turn them off. The more you’re slagging other people off to them, the more they’re going to start to think that you’re an antagonistic person, the more they are going to start to take other people’s sides, and the more they are going to distance themselves from you.

If you believe the psycho-babble then as an INFJ you are likely to judge others, to criticise them and to slam the door on them psychologically. That’s an awful lot of red nodes right there.

=== 29 June.md ===
# 29 June

2021

So the idea that clicked when you were listening to Robert Greene in prospect park yesterday is this: Queen Elizabeth sensed that as a woman she was in a precarious position, so she didn’t lead by force and coercion, rather her vulnerability lead her to a smarter style of leadership.

You are now a bit compromised. So you can’t stick your chest out and lord it over everyone. Maybe that’s a good way to think about it. You have to think twice now about pissing everyone off, you need people to really genuinely like the way you lead.

Other thing from Robert Greene was the whole “He who has a why, can bear with almost any how” thing. I.e. it’s not about building yourself a lifestyle, it’s about following your mission. Favela kids getting good at playing brass instruments in Rio de Janeiro.

Another thing, don’t forget that experience walking through the PATH train terminal at the World Trade Center. Just the whole thing of it being so beautiful, so well designed - people walking around on the floor above and then walking down to the platform. There’s something in there.

![29 March](images/29%20March.png)

2021

Slightly hungover day yesterday but at least created the 10 years vídeo for the upcoming otimismo planetario conference. Lovely seeing the early videos and the progression of the kids.

Toying with the idea of a 3+3+1 day cycle of business/program/curriculum x 2 then rest day Sunday. The criteria between business/program is asking “is this item contributing more directly to the day-to-day workings of the project or the business model that provides it with resources.”

Gives you a full-day run at whatever it is and a “day off” on Sunday (after the lessons, of course). This also gives you a night out on Saturday and a night in on Sunday.

Wednesday and Saturdays could be the deep-work (preferably green) tea days that you look forward to - your non-time “maker time” as opposed to the other days of “manager time”.

Just a little bit annoyed at Amelia’s COVID attitude - she’s off traveling and is basically in two others bubbles with Alison, Flor and Fabio. And us. This time really exposes the selfishness of people and the excuses that they use to cover it. She proclaims in saintly manner that she “wouldn’t judge anyone at this time” - which is a wonderful way of taking the moral high ground while fucking others over. 6% of deaths under 40 now.

Did a bike ride over the top yesterday and pretty much everything that could go wrong with the bike did go wrong. New rule: if the bike isn’t 100% you don’t ride it. This could save your life. Get a helmet, lights, a high-vis and a bell, dickhead. Legs absolutely destroyed at the end but still managed piano and trumpet practice at the end - well done me!

=== 3 Abril.md ===
# 3 Abril

2024

Things are getting tasty in the run up to Circo Voador. The advance online tickets ran out fast. 1.600 in a day. Then the discussions. Eventually went with Lencinho’s idea to tell everyone that their tickets do not guarantee entry, to avoid us effectively turning people away front the circo to guarantee entry for a bunch of people who end up flaking.

2022

**Daily nugget: Use the mouthpiece that gets you through the gig**

When you played with the squadronnaires you struggled partly because the 1.25 C made it hard work. For the sake of a slightly prettier sound in the solo, you sacrificed your overall professional performance. When you left, you could hardly get a decent reference.

You should use the mouthpiece which allows you to hold it together through the gig because tired chops sound worse than anything. Think about where else in life you could apply this principle: where else are you getting the priorities wrong and need to compromise? Where else are you obviously cracking important notes for the sake of subtleties that only you can hear?

=== 3 March.md ===
# 3 March

3 March

“I don’t have any distinction between weekdays and weekends, it’s all one for me. . . People sometimes view routines or habits in a negative way, “Wouldn’t it be great to be so free, to do whatever you want.” To me that’s like hell, like a nightmare. I would hate that. I want life to be relatively simple and digestible. Maybe that’s a weakness on my part. To me, routines and rituals are very liberating and soothing. I can’t imagine life without them.

- Robert Greene

2021

Just so satisfying to do meeze, trumpet and piano practice (Bach 1 round keys) in the evening. The thing about laying things out for the next day is so important for relaxing. Also make a mental note: since starting fasting in the evenings you been sleeping through till morning.

Loving the morning bike ride with strict time limit of 6:30 before turning back. You were about 100m off the caixa d’água today. I would place a fairly hefty bet on you finally making it all the way in 1 tomorrow. Art of manliness podcast the perfect companion. Mornings are bliss at the mo.

# 30 March

2021

Morning messed up by computer slowing down to a snails pace (had to delete a bunch of files and re-index spotlight but took me a while to get there), but made progress on these charts for the kids to play with projeto Guri (this is starting to feel like a drag but they are a big project: think impact of your materials).

When you finish half an hour of taking tunes round all 12 keys that’s like getting to the top of the hill on your bike: now you can just breeze down the other side admiring the scenery i.e. playing other tunes in their original key.

Piano is the best thing for your head. The favorite leisure activity. This is your baseline - “is this use of leisure time as good as playing piano?” Think how much you would love to sight read to a high standard on the piano, to fully understand a tune’s harmony just by playing it.

That’s the thing. The round the keys thing is the germane learning. It means that as you go on you start to understand tunes harmonically whatever key they are presented in and wherever they modulate to. It also means in the end you will play tunes from memory in different keys and have enough mental bandwidth left over to analyze the harmony as you go.

On a slightly less lofty note I just thought of the Tinder trick of offering to write them a new description. Fun, and very effective. Starting to think green tea has some kind of mystical quality for stimulating creativity. Coffee/black tea fit for cranking it out, green tea for divergent thinking - the real creative breakthroughs.

=== 30th November.md ===
# 30th November

30th November

2021

Listening to 4000 weeks. It’s the right book for the moment and very pertinent for you and your idleness averse, future-obsessed ways. The whole settling thing, accepting finitude, cultivating the joy of missing out. Coming to terms with the fact that it will always be like this.

Had the idea of hiring Cris as coordenador let’s hope she goes for it. Someone that will pitch in and that you like working with.

2020

Over the weekend been working on the first theory video, which is taking longer than expected. Need to keep on this though - the theory videos should help a lot, and the resulting keynote presentations ill be a great tool to use in the lessons as well. 

Went for long walks yesterday and Saturday with no headphones and had good ideas both days. Including going back to the Praça São Salvador idea on Saturdays (great visibility, perfect location, studio for drums, great bandstand for tiering sections) with the midweek being for individual lessons and sectionals. Use your house for classes, not big rehearsals. During the weeks you should have a grade 1 trumpet class, grade 4 sax. etc. etc. maybe even grade 1 theory, grade 3 keyboard harmony etc. The week should be about the classes and Saturday is showtime. Make Saturday an amazing public spectacle somewhere (maybe optional extra Sunday at Flamengo beach as well…)

Maybe a good start would be Saturday (praça SS) and Sunday (Flamengo beach) drop-ins with the volunteer teachers, aimed at the school kids. Later on Sunday could be an optional percussion with Mangueirinha plus instrumental lesson pull-outs. Becomes obligatory for kids who can’t do Sat.

The main recent development is that you’re now writing for full big band. There are a lot of good reasons for this:

1. A bigger band means a larger proportion of the students in the top bands - not just a small group having all the fun.
2. Reverse economics - the bigger the band the more students learning per director rehearsal hour.
3. Charts can be made much easier with a large band - backings put in sax section, easy lower brass parts.
4. There are much more youth big bands out there for us to do exchanges with. 
5. If we’re about playing in the street without mics, then we need that volume of sound from lots of players which also can balance a 4-5 piece percussion section.
6. Having drums + percussion means out percussionists can be learning drums as well.

If we say we’re starting a big band a year, that seems like a reasonable target (push to 5 tpts/5 troms/ 5 Perc)

Also, imagine if one day you manage to do a baile de carnaval with big band - maybe at circo voador / jubilee hall (for kids baile). That’s your annual fund raiser sorted! Get NYBB to come and do the pro band… TIME TO GET WRITING!

=== 31 Jan.md ===
# 31 Jan

31 Jan

“You can always tell a leader from the arrows in his ass.”

- Judah Folkman

DAILY NUGGET

Gallup Q12 (best predictors of performance):
1. Do you know what is expected of you at work?
2. Do you have the materials and equipment to do your work right?
3. At work, do you have the opportunity to do what you do best every day?
4. In the last seven days, have you received recognition or praise for doing good work?
5. Does your supervisor, or someone at work, seem to care about you as a person?
6. Is there someone at work who encourages your development?
7. At work, do your opinions seem to count?
8. Does the mission/purpose of your company make you feel your job is important?
9. Are your associates(fellow employees) committed to doing quality work?
10. Do you have a best friend at work?
11. In the last six months, has someone at work talked to you about your progress?
12. In the last year, have you had opportunities to learn and grow?

2022

Had a breakthrough in the morning. I always say this but I really think this is the format: tune related technical warm up exercises, then tune in standard notation, rest of arrangement bits, then a lookup chart for transposing melody to other key. After that I was pretty useless. It’s pretty relentless now and starting to grate that o just don’t get any days off at all in practice.

Good first rehearsal back in the favela and the materials worked a treat. Good turn out.

Favelagrafia want to do a recording with the kids. They want 10 kids from turma 1 to record a tune somewhere in a favela, but then it starts to become unclear.

Also the reference they sent was when you wish upon a star with Louis Armstrong which is all strings and vocal. Some of silly talk about “abrindo vozes” and assuming that I will do an arrangement for free. And the magic line about exposure for the project.

All in all not ideal but 2 problems for dismissing it: wouldn’t be good for relationship with kids in Fogueteiro or with Favelagrafia (who have already done us a favor), local project etc. Also, it’s you saying no to stuff, holding the project back from doing stuff.

Very tempted to just recommend them a string project in the nicest possible way. Would be nice to help them, but once we’ve said yes I’m worried they will take the piss in terms of COVID and how long we have to play for. And also, is this really going to work?

So there you have it. A nice juicy leader’s dilemma. Enough to stress you out and mess with your sleep last night. Mental note: you hate this stuff.

=== 4 October.md ===
# 4 October

2024

Rainy day in Engenho do Mato. In a routine of getting up at 5 every day, having a coffee and doing 25-30 mins of concentrated piano practice (Grieg poetic tone-picture no.6 at the moment). This brings you on as a musician - it’s just as important as arranging, and with the zero-tolerance aspect also serves as a mindfulness exercise. Thinking about maybe adding an extra step of composing a piece in a similar style after mastering each tune through the keys.

Just seen that Grieg’s lyric pieces were the most influential piano works during the belle époque and we even have them graded, starting from where you are:

This all started with your Dad’s final days where the music that helped most was the Arietta. One of those moments where you realize what you love - a moment of transcendence. From playing it badly on an out of tune piano at the funeral you now have until his 100th birthday to learn to compose your own lyric pieces.

With exactly 288 weeks left, you can dedicate 144 to mastering each of the 66 lyric pieces, then the following 144 to writing your own - the apprenticeship phase, followed by the creative-active. Remember, you can study Grieg all you like, but it will still come out as you.

Imagine if you also made enough money to buy the family a new Yamaha U3, or perhaps even a used grand. R$100.000 over 5 years gives roughly R$1.500 a month. Instead of a just a studio, create your music room. A big soundproofed , air-conditioned space where bands can play as well. 

2020

Moved to the upstairs flat which may actually be worse. Just no getting away from the noise of the road. Been managing to get work done although the whole dodgy Bluetooth keyboard/mouse connection to the Mac mini has been slowing things down.

Had a stressful Saturday worrying about getting the Banco do Brasil internet banking up and running (which involved cajoling Angelo and Melissa) and also coming clean to Amelia about the extra melodica videos. Even with a day’s distance these seem like small things that shouldn’t be giving you a day of stress. Anyway it all seemed to work out ok and the Sukiyaki video is looking and sounding great.

Thinking that it might not have been the best thing to do to get involved with Adrienne. It has been great, but worry that she’s going to get hurt. To be fair she’s so nice that she could be a contender. It’s just physically that I feel more of a fit with girls like Talita. She’s pressuring me to meet up today which I’m resisting. We went to the northeastern buffet place yesterday which was very nice indeed - and hot with the chilli sauce.

The house thing is a real bummer - it means you can’t really chill out at home. And the idea was that you’d be able to have some peace to chill out and work. Bit like the garage, but on the beach. In a quandary about whether to fork out another 1.500 for a decent place over the next couple of weeks, whether to even maybe move on to another place, or just find some way to spend as little time at home as possible.

Spent a lot of time on Airbnb but not had been hit by any inspiring options really. Also have to think a bit about when you want to start doing socially-distanced group things with favela brass and when you want to go back to the UK. My feeling is to to whatever traveling now and get back from the UK ready to go straight away early-mid Jan. Maybe break things up with one week out of aracaju?

Today is first day for a while with no coffee or tea. Brought it down gently last week with green tea. Feeling pretty lethargic and out of sorts now but nothing too much. Strange feeling of not wanting to do anything but not wanting to do nothing.

=== 4th December.md ===
# 4th December

4th December

No Enemies

By Charles Mackay

(English Chartist poet, 1814–1889)
 
YOU have no enemies, you say?	
  Alas! my friend, the boast is poor;	
He who has mingled in the fray	
  Of duty, that the brave endure,	
Must have made foes! If you have none,	       
Small is the work that you have done.	
You’ve hit no traitor on the hip,	
You’ve dashed no cup from perjured lip,	
You’ve never turned the wrong to right,	
You’ve been a coward in the fight.	        
 
As quoted by Margaret Thatcher to the Queen on Netflix, which I just watched on my first night back at home in Donny on the my fantastic new portable monitor and AKG headphones. It feels a little “cushy” to be taking a whole month out of Rio, but you can make it productive (recording the big band charts), and then you can have a clear shot at going straight through with the kids from January til July.

Started listening to Stalingrad on the way over, which was much more of a history book than I thought it was - for some reason I had it in my head that it was some kind of historical novel. Anyway fascinating stuff and in a strange way inspiring - what on earth do you have to complain about, compared to anyone who was involved on either side in that battle? 

Been a few days since I did the diary. There was the whole thing with Kayra - a learning experience I guess. Had a beer with Tom Le Mesurier who I have to say I don’t particularly like after the whole Somebody Feed Phil Thing - gives me the creeps now. Caught up with Bob over the phone - long overdue.

Cestas básicas from the Favelagrafia recording have arrived and I am just hoping that they don’t cause a kerfuffle. And Elber had decided that João Pedro should be going in for his Grade 1 in January when anyone with half a brain knows he’s somewhere between grade 2 and 4. Rafael also has not been using the books.

And now Talita wants to talk. This is your fault, you led her on. Either you’re in or you’re out my friend - doesn’t do anyone any good to be on the fence.

Dealing with the silly ideas of the board about the Circo Voador event (wristbands for all adults, obrigatory rental of ecocopos). Sômulo exposing himself as an absolute tyrant which might be a good thing: the other board members need to be alert to the danger of his becoming president and/or extending his term.

Sol has blocked Cris which is an ominous sign: a lawsuit is the last thing we need.

2023

Must be the time of year. It’s pretty full on here as well. Waiting for Lei Rouanet money, preparing for Paraty, orienting new team. Mum arrives tomorrow then you’re off to Florianopolis with Thamires as well. Unlike to be able to get too far from work. Have started drinking coffee and arranging in the mornings which is good but crowding out piano. 

2022

Long day. Admin marathon. It just comes in from all sides. You’re meditating and not drinking coffee, so you’re tired and stressed but still just about holding it together. Did have time to watch the first episode of Fargo series which was great.

It really does feel like you might burn out here.

Grim news from Ukraine.

2021

“Assim como o brasileiro foi educado para perder, o americano foi educado para ganhar.”
- Tom Jobim

Big day. Still working on format for instrument books and the micro-levels thing is looking great. Had the idea of dispensing even with the counting syllables and just using the image of the notes as lines against a counting grid: count the grid then play the rhythm. Do not forget this.

Long chat with Ed Matkin. He could be the partner for the instrumental grade books. If he could handle the selling part and a publisher the making and distributing, you could just write great method books and get paid for it. For me I like the idea of a joint brand with Ed, 50/50 after wherever the publisher takes. Passive income, Robert Kiyosaki would be proud. Of course he could sell you down the river too.

Posted Maria Rita playing Anunciação to thank FFT. Very good reception on Instagram. 

The Art of Impossible book making a big impact. Seems to have made me stop drinking. Gradually finding ways to cram all the daily weekly practices in and they definitely seem to be adding up to a better way of living and working.

=== 5 December-1.md ===
# 5 December

2022

After the initial success with having a day off coffee doing another one today. Headache hasn’t materialized but not much work has either. Yesterday was England vs Senegal at abcd with pre-match barbecue, so was going to be a slow day anyway.

Right. Listening to the 7 rules of power and the penny has dropped: you need a rougher edge - you need to stop worrying about what people think. You can’t keep everyone happy and you will never be able to make an omelette without breaking eggs. They play dirty, you need to stand your ground.

Speak less, use more direct language. Say what needs to be said. They want you to **lead them to victory**: competence, boldness, confidence. Be wrong sometimes, make enemies. Tune in to your rebel days at school: you’re going to die - why not test the limits?

2021

In a bad mood. Sunday night and staying in at Selina. Had BCS event on Saturday, then beers and pizza, then aterro this morning, then nobody turned up to Cacilda so you went for a drink with Tadeu.

The method is in a good place. All you need to do now is crank out more tunes and references. Transition to tea before you fall out with too many people. It’s done.

It seems like you always think that you have finally settled on the right format, then you go and change it. However, even with that caveat, this current set up does look good with the group method technical warm up, then the figurenotes tunes  transposing into 2 keys, and the patterns warm up as well. Think you may have cracked it

=== 5 July.md ===
# 5 July

2024
At danger of entering into dangerous water with Pat. She’s taken on this other job with Rede Cruzada and the feeling is that she’s not giving it her all with Favela Brass. The other feeling is that there’s an element of her wanting to do what you don’t want her to do (writing projects, liasing with the patrocinador) and not wanting to do what you do want her to do (updating the budget spreadsheet).

It’s not all-out warfare, but you need to work on this relationship. As much as anything, whether you like it or not, she has the power to bad-mouth you to her friend at PRIO, Camilla.

Yesterday you went to PRIO asking for instruments, when it turns out that you still have space in the budget. You just hadn’t gone into Raissa’s budget in time to verify that we really do have a surplus. Pat could snitch on that. Just be smart about it and don’t draw attention to it.

Worried about your memory. Had some senior moments recently that were different from before: forgetting the topic of conversation mid-conversation. Anything that can be done to mitigate this would be great: lots of exercise, less booze and less caffeine would seem good places to start.

Listening to “Coming Up for Air” for a second time: this is really the book you were looking for. What you really dread is the idea of being an incompetent leader that makes life hard for your team. With the recommendations in the book you have the chance to make things better in this respect - go for it!

=== 5 June.md ===
# 5 June

2023

Fantastic day at Itacoatiara beach yesterday with Thamires. Water just right for swimming, listening to the Sony stereo speakers made all the difference. Stayed there from 08:30 to 15:30 and didn’t have any idea we were there so long. At points, you managed to put the work stuff out of your mind and be in the moment. Meditation is there for you to be able to do this.

One thing that came to mind while swimming was that perhaps there is an element missing to all of this 4000 weeks stuff about not spending life just pursuing goals the whole time. That element being the simple idea of rhythms of tension and release in life. If we want to enjoy life, then working towards goals and then relaxing a bit, then working towards the next one is a satisfying rhythm. 

Yes it’s a bit like we’re on a treadmill, but it’s a virtuous cycle - we set up a goal about how things could be a bit better, get at it (tension), then go to the beach, drink and listen to music (release). We spend our lives engaged it the pleasurable business of making life slightly better. The problem for you has not been so much that you’re living a goal-oriented life - that’s what gives life meaning - but rather the workload has been so high that even in the moments that should be in release, you’re in tension worrying about what’s not getting done.

To get the tension x release thing right you not only have to have release, but you have to set it up by working well in tension. Really get at it. The worst feeling in the world is that you kind of drifted when you should have been working, so the release hasn’t been earned. Think about being at uncle Paul’s with Dad: you were working during the day to earn your BBQ at night, and that’s why you have such a happy memory of that time.

Think about the stress of Favela Brass (and dealing with Pam) as part of the tension. You endure all sorts of difficulty during the week - pressure, difficult decisions, wrong decisions, embarrassment, self-doubt, petty politics, anger  -  in the service of a good cause,  and in doing so earn the right to go to the beach at the weekend and spend hours on end drinking and relaxing in the sun.

If you run away from the tension, you’ll never enjoy the release.

2022

Rehearsal at CIEP despite still testing positive for COVID. Started Marcelo on trumpet, Vinicio on trombone, Rian on sax, and Zuri is starting on trombone as well. Really this lesson can run with just you, Joe and Mangueirinha at a push. You can start mixed groups of beginners off, then take the band for the last 30 mins.

Cancelled Cacilda - hardly any students, it’s inside, and after the rehearsal I was just completely knackered. Think this might be it for Cacilda. It’s just too much. Organizing an oficina is kind of social, but only if you actually have students. Take Sunday back.

“Pay it forward, because you can’t pay it back.”

Learned that one the hard way.

=== 5 November.md ===
# 5 November

2024

Yesterday accepted the “de cria para cria” award at the câmara municipal with Henri. Seemed so tribal (the tribe in question not being yours) and was nice to be out of there. Still Favela Brass now has a pretty certificate.

Much more interestingly, stumbled on the solfege methods by Dannhäuser and Lavignac, and also Eileen Sauer’s page (prompted by the MTB tests asking students to sing intervals). Maybe an hour of rhythm reading and theory on one side, and an hour of solfege, harmony and improvisation on the other.

2023

Léo the builder is putting a new roof on upstairs - so far seems like he knows what he’s doing.

The business with the neighbours is leaking back in. In a nasty situation with the Mums this could be used against you and probably already is. As Mangueirinha says, the danger is not the lawsuit, it’s the rumours. You’re doing the right thing - make the project less dependent on you, set up your home outside the favela, gradually take the project to the schools.

The tricky part is the role of Cris in this. She’s slippery, and doesn’t mind playing dirty. She is probably playing you and the mums off against each other to some degree. A good idea would be to take the time to talk to the difficult mums. Remember, Tom, Cris isn’t pure evil, but you can’t let your guard down. The difficult thing is that now she’s got a gun to your head. All you can do is keep calm and carry on - don’t run from the dogs or attack them, just pick up a stick and keep walking.

…Actually it’s not just about keeping calm and carrying on. It’s also about using this to become a better person. That’s the story here. Remember your red letter to yourself? You got to that point because this failure spurred you on. Use your regrets, remember the photo film negatives. You need stoic philosophy to get you through this, and then that will help you get through anything. You have to be truly brave here. A problem is a chance to do your best.

Started work on “when you wish” with the kids. Just the troms, just the trumpets, then just Katarina. Great to be getting them reading, counting and playing in harmony. Have to admit to being more than a little bit proud of the arrangement. Write more.

=== 5 October.md ===
# 5 October

2023

Amazing how much you can learn in a year: Cris as Executive Director? But also amazing how far you have come in this respect: you now have a good executive producer in Pat, 2 good production assistants in Carol and Iris, communications coordinator in Maria Carolina, and a full teaching staff that can basically do the lessons without you. Once a week just to work on theory, impro etc. and tidy up the new tune is fine. That day when Jim Trott visited the lessons and commented on how you really are on your own was a bit of a wake up call - would be great to send him a video of the lessons now with everything running without you.

The big difference is that you now have Thamires and the chalet in Engenho do Mato. Life after the favela has now taken a very concrete form and there’s no going back. You’ve been writing less diaries because you’ve been living more - you have someone to share things with now. Time off isn’t spent wondering what to do with the time off - you’re at the beach, sharing BBQs, even just watching TV together. And the vision in terms of where all this is going for you is more pratical: you don’t suddenly hand over the reigns to another executive director and expect to be able to hide in the music part and everything be alright, or leave Favela Brass altogether. Rather, it’s a case of getting the thing running more or less smoothly and gradually handing tasks off to trusted staff across all areas. Going from head cook and bottle washer, to hands-off boss, to what you always wanted to be: (paid) arranger.

2022

Last year’s diary a bit of a hammer blow. But anyway…

If I have this right I think today may be a bit of a red letter day. I think I have finally seen the way out of this (and I really wasn’t seeing one before). You don’t farm out the teaching and leave the Favela - that way is expensive as hell and who, realistically, is going to be able/willing to take over at the assunção. It’s strange.

Walking back down from jogging up past CEAT it hit me - you stay in the favela, but you just offload the executive director responsibilities, and gradually more and more of the teaching. You end up giving lessons in the favela in the evenings, doing shows, making course materials, overseeing the teaching, that’s it. No more bullshit from the parents, no more bullshit from Camila, no more bullshit from the board. As Kenny said, the music is the fun bit.

Big question is who takes over as executive diretor but surely Cris would be favorite as she wouldn’t take it in the wrong direction. Could do a trial year, starting with the new Rouanet cycle in March. The board may wish to widen the search, and that would be fine as well.

Point is you’re doing 2 jobs - executive director and teacher - and it’s holding the project back on both fronts. You want to be creating content, not dealing with people problems - leave that to people who relish that kind of work. You’ll have time for Brassify and Tube Map Scales and whatever you else create. You’ll be positioning yourself for other opportunities, the next project.

And yes, at some point maybe you’ll work out how to farm out the teaching at the assunção and head off full tilt on the next adventure, but you’ll do that knowing that Favela Brass is well and truly set up. There’s much more on the music side that has to be you than on the admin side, so you should leave that till last. You leaving the favela and/or not doing lessons at the assunção would derail the project.

You were feeling trapped because in the favela you’re too up close and personal with the parents etc. but as artistic director it’s a bit different. They just won’t deal as much with you. You make clear that you’re just teaching and it takes the pressure off. That way you keep the house and never fall out with the favela. It gradually just morphs away from being your project. That’s the point, it stops being your project.

But seriously, how cool would that be? - no more board meetings or committee meetings, no more Whatsapp groups. Cris for dealing with people and Raissa for actually getting the admin done. Fátima still around for the experience. 

Would also open up the possibility of a bit of work at the British School if you wanted it and the odd extended leave. By leaving slowly you avoid the whole thing collapsing when you have to leave suddenly at some point, of you choosing between being trapped or betraying the project, your students, the favela.

Demoting yourself will reduce the jealousy and in a strange way put you in the driving seat. Now Cris can’t blame all the difficult decisions on you. She takes the heat and you’re just the one that they’re all dependent on for holding things together musically. And you don’t have to worry too much because you’re not trapped - once the ED role is filled and things are rolling without you on the admin side, you’re already on the off-ramp. Really, the problem is getting someone decent to accept the ED role, and the board to accept a different ED.

Damn, it’s not far off: work on materials in the day then test them on the kids at night. Tuesday, Thursday, Saturday  Sunday nights free. If and when one day you have kids you could even go as low as one night a week in the favela plus shows and you live where you want. The whole Tube Map Scales thing is so fun: this is where you’re at - Brassify can be even more rewarding, and really is right on your purpose. You need to carve time to get going on these things.

Me as the director of a big project living in the favela isn’t sustainable. But you change the first part of that rather than the second. You could even at some point put yourself as just musical director in the Pereira unidade. 

And with the ED role taken it’s much easier to take an offer abroad - every week the course materials get stronger and it’s easier for the lessons to run without you.

When Jim Trott came round it was a moment of clarity - you’re not an executive director if you’re taking the band. You have to go one way or the other, and it’s becoming pretty clear which one suits your talents most.

I think move more quickly on this. Next March - could make it a trial year. Talk about it in the upcoming strategy meeting. Just thinking about this took a huge weight off. There’s a light at the end of the tunnel now.

2021

It’s still there. Imagine yourself as Dad, knowing you’re on your last legs, sitting waiting for your favorite son to tell you that he’s off back to Brazil - that he can’t wait around for you to die. As he said, it’s so painful. Nobody deserves that.

Looking to clean up the act a bit when I get back to Rio. Stop the boozing till carnaval dates and maybe cut down the caffeine as well. Meditation, exercise etc.

I also discovered something important about trumpet practice: it’s all about consistency. Total consistency. Just 30 mins a day and you can be just about hitting top Fs. BUT it has to be every day every day every day. It’s not about the days on - it’s about NEVER HAVING A DAY OFF. What other things are like that?

=== 6 Jan (2).md ===
# 6 Jan (2)

2023

**Christmas Past**

You grew up a star student, with a great talent for music. A bit of a loner, and shy with girls, but that helped with the practice time. Found a solid group of friends in the Doncaster Youth Jazz Orchestra and had some great experiences doing shows and foreign trips. Enjoyed economics at school and ended up studying Management rather than music at uni. Dreams of being an investment banker during the day and Groove Armada by night.

From uni onwards was a bit of a lost period. You got gigs with the Squadronnaires and some live PA stuff, but it was a time marked by loneliness and a lack of professional success. However many months it was at Uncle Paul’s working on an electronic music album that never happened, then a couple more years in Manchester living alone trying to find the lost chord, then about 4 years in London with grand projects including starting a big band, which never amounted to anything. Not taking the plunge with girls lead to getting even more behind on that front.

By the end you were turning into a bit of a weirdo, living in that depressing shared house in Wembley, getting so het up about little things like house cleaning rotas and bigger things, like having frittered an inheritance, that the low point was you having a panic attack. Another daft project, to save live music by moving to Rio de Janeiro and starting a big band, led you to sell everything and buy tickets to Brazil (not without trying to chicken out).

On arriving in Rio life improved a lot. Your musical skills were finally put to use in Rodas de Samba, Carnaval etc., and even though the big band didn’t happen a lot of good things did and you really did get a lot closer to what were were searching for all along - live music as a part of popular culture. After a very slow start with the girls, as you entered your 30s you started dating and having longer-term relationships. A succession of gorgeous girls who you wouldn’t have dreamt of before, but you didn’t commit to any of them.

About 4 years in, with you about 32 you moved to a Pereirão and started Favela Brass. A very good cause filling a genuine gap. For about 7 years it was a you+ project, then during lockdown you put a board together and finally cracked the funding thing, allowing you to give up the part-time job that you hated at the British School. In 2022 you successfully executed the first Rouanet project and secured funding for the next. The band got much better and after wasting a lot of time on wacky methodologies you finally got a solid band program going.

**Christmas Present**
**
**
Right now you find yourself pulled in different directions. The founder period of Favela Brass is well and truly over and now it’s a management job, which doesn’t seem to suit your skill set. It’s all cut-throat politics and tricky decisions, rather than teaching and arranging. Living in the Favela where you work seems more claustrophobic every day and the idea of raising kids there becomes ever less attractive. You want out of the admin side at the very least and now the money is here it looks like you have a chance to do it gracefully.

Post-Talita the dating situation has been slow, and time seems to be catching up with you. 43 is old to be dating, and even if you met Mrs Right (who doesn’t exist) tomorrow, you would be running after kids in your late 40s and probably into your 50s. Work has been so intense that it really has been difficult to spend time going out and meeting new people. However, living in Pereira and being with Favela Brass is still streets ahead of how life was in the lost years before Brazil. You have status and friends here, a reasonable income and a respectable, useful job with responsibility.

Losing Dad in 2021 was a huge blow which threw many things into sharp relief - mainly that you didn’t get on with life in the sense of having a family. He never got to meet his grandchildren on your side, never got to go to your wedding, or see you provide a solid home for your children. After all the tilting at windmills, you didn’t hit the basics and those foundational shortcomings are coming home to roost. Mum is also on her own now and Oli’s already overwhelmed with his own family, which makes it seem increasingly tricky to leave her on her own as time goes on - the other thing you learned from Dad’s death is that you need to start thinking about other people for once.
**
**
Many people end up in much worse places at 43 and if you died tomorrow, you have done something with your life: Favela Brass. Cherry’s done, now for the cake.
**
**
**Christmas Future**

Criteria:

1. Finding a girl 
2. Looking after Mum
3. Getting back to music / arranging
4. Brassifying the world
5. Supporting/raising a family

Mum Options:
1. Moving back to Donny in 5-10 years.
2. Moving somewhere closer to Donny. Even Paris (Eurostar) or Portugal (Manchester Airport).

Let’s have some fun. This is what is in the back of your mind: a 1-year project involving lots of European cities. You could take a Brazilian girl with you. Imagine you are backpacking. Donny, Paris, Lyon, Berlin (Roman), London, Manchester, Rome (Alberto), Madrid (Joe), Washington DC (Joe), 

Have to find a manager for each of the bands - the musos won’t keep it going. And what about the unis thing? That could work in the UK as well.

Everything takes longer than planned 

Think positive! What do you need to start a band? One musician from the city who knows other musicians who are good and interested, and a place to play. Money to pay for rehearsals.

You could get a Brazilian to live with you in Portugal, and it wouldn’t be the end of the world. If it was a French girl you could live in Paris. I think you could pull a French girl. Could you try a year in Paris?

Number 2 means that in about 7-10 years you’ll have to move back to Donny, or close enough to visit regularly. Now, if you find a girl and stay in Brazil

Mum moving to Sunderland won’t work because Oil’s got too much on his plate already, and she needs to be near her friends.

You could do Brazil in the school holidays, that’s something.

That means kids going to school in South Yorkshire unless you see another plan. Think about Nanny Roo - she was unhappy on her own and had to move in with Mum or Charlotte later on. You could maybe just live close i.e. Sheffield.

So you need a girl who’s willing to move to Donny or Sheffield. And you need to think about how you could construct a life worth living there, as Mum inevitably marches on towards 95 (by which time you will be 68). 

Could you live in Donny and travel lots to make it bearable? Not really with small kids. Also travelling up to Donny frequently with a young family would be tiring. Oh Christ.

***

There’s the *grass is greener* effect at work here 

…

So what could satisfy all that lot?

Stay in Rio and tough it out till you find a lady

…

Brassify:

The next project idea is here, but is it a good one? Yes, doing the arrangements is practical, starting a band is doable (providing you get the workload down at Favela Brass). But where is this going?

Where do you want to get to with this?

You getting paid to write brass band arrangements for a bunch of bands around the world.

Bad outcome:

You get the arrangements done and the band sounds ok but you can’t really find a way to pay good musicians, let alone yourself. A bunch of decent videos of arrangements on Youtube don’t really attract much attention. It’s just another fanfarra, another project that doesn’t get off the ground.

Good outcome:

The band in Rio is a hit and you manage to set them up as a going concern. You then take it to other cities where you set up even better bands who rock it. More and more bands start using your arrangements. Slow work, but eventually you start getting in demand as an arranger and musical director.

Rouanet

This is a project that could be approved in Rouanet. At least the band part.

# On 4000 Weeks

Burkemann’s thesis is that instrumentalizing our time, especially our leisure time, is a problem. That we need to embrace the fact that we’re just not going to get everything done, therefore we should just chill out and choose something realistic to get done, forgetting the rest. That we’re spoiling our lives by overestimating the importance of what we do with them.

Having a band to play the charts is a good start. Favela brass can handle some but not all. A pro band could be fun and make a bit of cash. Look at James. Running a band is people and stress, yes, but nothing on a nonprofit. And it’s fun and friends as well.

2019

Thinking more seriously about the idea of doing an online iPGCE. With that, your CV starts to look quite good for teaching jobs at international schools. The option of extending it to an MA is also tempting (have to find a way to finance it).

A full-time job at an international school would give you financial security, a good school to send your kids to and also a potential stream of students to join your extra-curricular programs. Indeed, what makes this seem like a viable option is the idea that Favela Brass is moving towards the idea of a 2:30pm - 5:30pm extracurricular band program at CIEP. No reason why private school students couldn’t be a (paying) part of that, or why you couldn’t do the same thing for TBS students on Tuesdays & Thursdays.

Yes, it would mean a lot of time giving lessons for rich kids and less “free” time for self-development. But remember that all teachers have free periods and all you would have to do is buy a laptop. The melodica lessons that currently happen at 12H and 14:30H could be covered by other teachers, so you would be looking at 7:30 - 15H in the schools, followed by 15:30-17:30 at CIEP, then maybe 18:30 - 20:30 in the favela. It’s a lot, but remember all the public holidays, lost days and the fact that it all stops for July and January.

David Brennan made a point about doing things while you have time. At the moment you don’t have kids or a wife - that may not always be the case. It does seem like a good time to do this. Sometimes you just have to move in the right general direction. Take Talita’s advice: get yourself qualified.

=== 8 September.md ===
# 8 September 

2022

Listening to “The Antidote” got me thinking. Imagine you are o seeing yourself (and, crucially, everyone else) in some kind of a miniature live board game. What is different about seeing life from this perspective? What differences does this make in the way you would act? How you experience life?

It’s all in the ego and the self. That detachment makes for a much healthier way of seeing yourself and others. You are still charged with controlling your “character”, still rooting for you, still wanting you to have fun. But makes things a bit less personal. You’re more resilient.

At certain time you will be inescapably drawn into your character’s first-person perspective. When you are playing well, this will be in moments of inspiration, flow  and connection. When things aren’t going so well it will be in moments of anger, pain and rumination.

Ah, and a less profound insight. Over exercising reliably makes you feel much better.
