Weekend they come to you. Non-exclusive groups would be good so they can be playing Saturday and Sunday if they want.

=== 8th Jan.md ===
# 8th Jan

**8th Jan**

2021

On the plane back to Rio via Paris now. Time to think about the upcoming year…

**2021 WIGs**
If you were only allowed 2 WIGs for 2021 what would they be? I would say number 1 create and record a big band repertoire and number 2 get a massive melodica program going in the schools. There are other things, like sorting the syllabus and exams, but these are the 2 things that would make the most difference. Why?

**WIG 1: Big Band Arrangements**
These arrangements are the mission statement of the project. Get these done and you have thrown the gauntlet down for what we want to achieve. Doing the videos with the kids during lockdown is ideal for keeping both the kids’ energy up (and challenging them) and also having stuff to share on social media. The arrangements also open the door for international exchange collaborations and collaborations with famous artists. Staff will get a bit of glory.

If you get a decent book together this year (42 pearlers?) then 2022 can be about getting stuff played weekly by students, staff exchange partners, pro musician friends, adult students etc…  hopefully down at the coreto moderno on Sundays. You will learn loads from making the recordings in terms of arranging and also playing the individual instruments.

**WIG 2: Mass Melodica Participation.**
The limiting factor at the moment is the quality and quantity of our students. We have great volunteer teachers, we have instruments coming out of our ears, what we don’t have is a decent-sized waiting list of students that are hungry to learn and will practice at home. If we want to have a generation of great musicians coming out of the project in 8-10 years time, then we have to sow the seeds now. Only a small proportion of students will complete melodica and recorder karate, we know that, so we need to cast the net very wide. 

If 1 in 10 of the 1500 kids in our schools now achieved that during 2021 we would have a bumper year to get our Rouanet money invested in. Imagine if in 2022 every one of our schools had an extra-curricular music program with melodica/recorder, percussion, and graded group wind instrument sessions. Open bloco rehearsals at Praça São Salvador on Saturdays and Praia do Flamengo Sundays before big band will work well with larger groups - remember being in an empty Quadra at CIEP? It’s all about big mo so let’s go!

**2021 Habits**
Last year was a lot about assuming the role of Executive Director, not being a perfectionist and generally getting to grips with the management aspect. With lockdown you established the solid 30 mins of trumpet and piano daily, and towards the end of the year read the work clean book from which first the main wildly important new habit for 2021 comes: the daily meeze. The second WIH is a 75-minute writing big-band arrangement writing session followed by a 30 minute recording session.

Typical day:
6H up, meditate, exercise, brekky, tea!
8H Meeze
8:30 Writing session
9:45 Tea Break
10H Recording
10:30 Piano
11H Last tea and hit the list!

**WIH 1: Daily Meeze**
The reason for the daily meeze is that we want this year to be the year of getting organised. You have always wanted to be on top of things, to feel on top of things. The Meeze is the way to do that because it means you get the things done that need to be done. It’s the difference between being organised and not being organised. The difference between being someone with lists and someone without lists. And.. it’s a new habit which will mean you will feel a real difference.

**WIH 2: Big Band Arranging**
This is your deep work for the day and it’s your creative product at the end of the year. Imagine that: a big band book with recordings of all the tunes and videos of the best ones including some of the kids and a variety of other guest appearances. We can push the deadline till the end of your Christmas break next year so that you get the last month of recording at home.

Think about it: it’s like you’re releasing multiple albums - you have never released anything creatively before now. Finished product. And it’s bang on your wider mission with the potential to expand your impact way beyond Rio. Stay on this, just this. Your weakness is that you have good ideas but don’t see them through. This year you’re seeing this through.

Mate I reckon you need to up your age limit to a strict 23 absolute minimum.

2021

I’m grateful for having a loving, supporting, cultured, musical, good, unbroken family. I’m grateful for my amazing house with stunning view of yellowy sunrise this morning.

I’m grateful for the gift of my own intelligence. Whatever bum cards nature dealt you, you got it where it counts. It’s the number one thing for human beans and it means you are capable of amazing things if you manage to get your ducks in a row. Really, thank your lucky stars.

The flow exercises are paying off. Virtuous circle happening with meditation starting to come into it, then practicing your weaknesses (which is really good keep this going). Haven’t drunk for a couple of weeks either.

Doing these 8-to-a-grade Folhas and tested trombone ones with Nathan and Henri and they worked a treat. Thinking along the lines that if different music projects and schools could only agree to a given standard for each colored fita, that would be a great thing for Brazilian music Ed in itself. That would be a great legacy - to bring music grades to Brazil.

=== 9 Feb.md ===
# 9 Feb

**9 Feb**

2023

By coincidence I thought roughly the same thing again today: « please make it go away » - that was after a rambling board meeting about new directors where we really didn’t get anywhere (after a day of admin, Saara and with the Super Baile Brass looming). Really sat there in the meeting and thought « I just do no want to be here ». How great would it be not to be the ED - and how much better could someone else do the job?

Struck by the humanity in the photo of the Turkish guy holding the hand of his 15 year-old daughter under the rubble. Humanity. Being human. Isn’t that what it comes down to? Isn’t that what you need to cultivate?

2022

Another non-stop, please make it stop day. Luuk Hof over for lunch. Cancelled the lesson because it was raining on and off. Wish I hadn’t so we could have got cracking on the Anita arrangement.

Yesterday, after ringing me outright Bindu left a long audio message which after 2 minutes finally came to the point: she wants to put her produtora friend on the board. Happy happy joy joy. Someone to beat me over the head with.

Played “La Cloche Sonne” for the first time tonight and it made me think of the inexorable clock that’s ticking for all of us. This is your midlife time - where what had heretofore been a distant spectre starts to become a tangible figure, coming into sharper focus by the year. The regrets also start to take a more solid form, as more and more of the irreversibles start to pile up and bother you:

2021

Beware Stugger. Though he was your best friend for a long time and has been very supportive of the project, you cannot ignore the signs that you can’t trust him. Remember the terrible impact that Carola had, working behind the scenes, and bear in mind that they, coincidentally, ended up together (essentially against you). Remember how he left you for dead on last day of the coast to coast walk, his little comment to Sally at Carnaval, the latent hate that spilled out with the failed UK trip, and his “Amelia is going to hate you after this” slip. Remember him taking the Matt Dabbs donation and not even telling you, putting up an ad for instruments for “Favela Brass and Gracie’s school”, and remember him quietly not mentioning Rob Egerton’s instrument donation.

In Robert Greene terms you have to wake up to this and, without overreacting, manage the situation. What decisions can you take now to limit the damage Stu’s ego can cause? It’s two-pronged really - you have to keep him sweet, and you have to keep him at a distance. Keeping him sweet means bending a little bit, buttering him up, massaging that raging ego. Keeping him at a distance means not asking him, NYBB or DYJO for help with anything (OK you can borrow a Bari sax from Stu Macdonald!), letting the board members know the situation in an indirect way, and also arranging other, better, exchanges and exchange partners - take the initiative and forge other, less complicated partnerships.

He definitely has shades of the “Relentless Rebel” outlined below, and this explains his slightly conflicted attitude to you. In some ways you embody this rebel attitude - rejecting a possible career in financial services to create an independent project in a favela. He wants to be a part of this and he genuinely wants to support the cause. But he is also becomes a simmering cauldron of resentment at the first sign of any successful authority on your part. He wants to build you up, but he also wants to tear you down - just as he wanted to tear down Dennis Rollins, Cast, DYJO’s secretary, their ex-treasurer, and the board as a whole if they dare to question him.

The thing is to take other initiatives that don’t involve Stugger. Dilute his influence. Look elsewhere. Make videos with other projects, lay the groundwork for other exchanges. Raise money elsewhere. And keep him away from the others - he won’t be able to bear you gaining their respect. Also, work on those that he might infect. If he recruits help for us make sure that you thank them profusely at the time and remember them afterwards - don’t hand him the opportunity. Rob Egerton, Sam Thornton, NYBB, Encontro. You must protect your reputation from attack.
 
It seems sad to be writing all this about a friend, but there is also a certain sense of relief in looking at this objectively. Who knows, if you get it right then maybe you two will be able to relax and enjoy a beer at Carnival.

**The Arrogant and Proud Man:**

Although he may initially disguise it, this man’s touchy pride makes him very dangerous. Any perceived slight will lead to a vengeance of overwhelming violence. You may say to yourself, “But I only said such-and-such at a party, where everyone was drunk. . . .” It does not matter. There is no sanity behind his overreaction, so do not waste time trying to figure him out. ***If at any point in your dealings with a person you sense an oversensitive and overactive pride, flee. Whatever you are hoping for from him isn’t worth it.***

**The Hopelessly Insecure Man:**
**
**
This man is related to the proud and arrogant type, but is less violent and harder to spot. His ego is fragile, his sense of self insecure, and if he feels himself deceived or attacked, the hurt will simmer. He will attack you in bites that will take forever to get big enough for you to notice. If you find you have deceived or harmed such a man, disappear for a long time. Do not stay around him or he will nibble you to death.

**From Robert Greene 10 Toxic Types to avoid hiring at any cost:**
**
**
**The Relentless Rebel: **
*
*
At first glance such people can seem quite exciting. They hate authority and love the underdog. Almost all of us are secretly attracted to such an attitude; it appeals to the adolescent within us, the desire to snub our nose at the teacher. They don’t recognize rules or precedents. Following conventions is for those who are weak and stodgy. These types will often have a biting sense of humor which they might turn on you, but that is part of their authenticity, their need to deflate everyone, or so you think. But if you happen to associate with this type more closely you will see that is something they cannot control; it is a compulsion to feel superior, not some higher moral quality.

In their childhood a parent or father figure probably disappointed them. They come to mistrust and hate all those in power. In the end, they cannot accept any criticism from others because that reeks of authority. They cannot ever be told what to do. Everything must be on their terms. If you cross them in some way, you will now be painted as the oppressor and be the brunt of their vicious humor. They gain attention with this rebel pose and soon become addicted to the attention. ***In the end it is all about power — no one shall be above them and anyone who dares will pay the price.*** Look at their past history — they will tend to split with people on very bad terms, made worse by their insults. Do not be lured in by the hipness of their rebel pose. Such types are eternally locked in adolescence and to try work with them will prove as productive as trying to lock horns with a sullen teenager.
  

=== 9 July.md ===
# 9 July

2023

Baile Brass yesterday with To be Wild and Metais Pesados was lovely. Kids played great, and just such a great interaction with the guest musicians. Felt a bit bad pushing the battle of the bands thing - really did feel like a little bit of a humiliation for the adults. Hiding Cacilda at the beginning was fun too. And coming home to drink cointreau and cream with Thamires was the best possible end to the night.

There’s always something, and it’s Pam at the moment. She’s clearly on a warpath against both you and Cris. She seems to be splitting the team into the pros (her and Sassá, maybe Camila), and the incompetents (you and Cris). She’s trying to lay down the law with you about budgets and generally busting your balls in front of the others at any opportunity.

At this point, her becoming executive director is a bad outcome for you unless you’re going to walk away from Favela Brass completely: but even then, would Favela Brass thrive under her, or would you be back picking up the pieces? Maybe that’s what you do: walk away and let her piss everyone off in your absence. Then come back in and put her in her place, by popular demand. 

Listened to the Robert Green chapter on one-upmanship, because I think the best strategy would be to get Pam to melt down. The problem with firing her is the idea of you being childish and truculent, getting rid of competent people on a whim. Yes, you can make the decision not to hire her next year (or even cut her loose before), but so much better if you are reluctantly letting her go after it becomes clear that she’s driving everyone crazy.

Just looked at the latest torrent of emails and in there is one of her saying that the association has to pick up the tab if we take parents to any gigs, because there’s nothing in Rouanet about transporting parents. I think she thinks that by making you request association money from the diretoria for your silly idea, she’ll make you look like a clown. If you can get Fátima to back you up, this could be a good opportunity for the one-upmanship dynamic to play out: you need to be the one maintaining your cool while she lashes out.

Your weak point is that you don’t want to have to pick up Pam’s responsibilities. And another danger is you and Pam coming before the board like two arguing siblings. A key component is her overplaying her hand: thinking that she can turn the board and staff against you by trash-talking you, so that people come to the conclusion that she’s the problem.

Plan A now should be running the year out, but not hiring her again next year. Options include Sassá as coordenador geral, or someone else with experience with Rouanet. With that in mind you must now:

- Stop the trash-talking of other employees to Pam, or of Pam to other employees.
- Be organised, professional. Respond to the emails. Add value, work hard. Be nice.
- Subtly challenge Pam’s authority and stoke her insecurities when you can - get her to leak all of that contempt and arrogance. 
- Try to get one other person that thinks she should go: Cris would be an obvious choice.
- Work on everyone, but especially Sassá.

The thing with Pam is that she’s willing to pick a fight with anyone: PRIO, you, the diretoria. But she is also competent and organised and people come to rely on that. You need everyone to be feeling drained from her constant pressuring and confrontation - you need everyone counting the days for her to leave.

Try to get inside her head as well - how’s she seeing this? What are her plans? She must be thinking about elbowing you out and firing Cris. How does she go about do that? Make Cris and you look bad in front of everyone, including the diretoria. Make her look good to the diretoria, for example by saving them money. Get to the point where she’s running everything with the staff and the staff want you out of the way.

Dude, you’re going to wake up tomorrow with all this crap hanging over, but just remember that it’s all good learning about human nature, you can only do your best, and keeping a sense of humour is always the best policy.

Today you spent hours sorting out the FB repertoire books: this will help loads. Whatever happens, don’t let all this crap distract you from your music.
 
2021

Just watched the Talented Mr. Ripley. Not comfortable viewing. All about people with terrible secrets. It must be coming. Too many people in the favela know about the thing with the neighbors. You can’t keep this away from the board forever - especially now Bindu is on the case.

All you can do is see if there’s any way to ameliorate things, try and draw a line under it, do your best to make as much positive impact as you can with the project, and live a little of the Brazil dream while it lasts. Might be 40 years might be 40 days, so embrace it. Be nice to people, share lots of smiles and love and music.

This theory of change diagram has taken on an extra dimension. You REALLY WANT to make this change - it’s not just a diagram for a grant. Make something real tomorrow.

All this worry. Pour it into your work. That’s your only hope at redemption. You started favela brass because you were ashamed of yourself. Now make it into a success. Use this. Hard work and humility - nobody can take that away from you. Lose your ego, find your purpose.

Let the board pay you more than the rest of the team.

You’ve made the decision to stay in the DE role for the rest of the year. Be a good stoic and put your back into it now - stop looking around.

Didn’t go to the lessons at the Assunção today. That’s a turn-up. As things are you’re only committed to one lesson a week - if you’re in this for the long haul then something has to give.

2022

Mum’s 70th. Cake and schloer and presents in the hotel reception with Oli and Charlotte, then lunch at the Shard and a terrible show later on - the play that goes wrong. Christ that was bad.

Spent a lot of the day stewing because Raissa has put Cris as “produtora de todo o projeto incluindo alocação com parceiros e alunos” or something like that on the Rouanet orçamento. Something tells me you aren’t flavour of the month with  the staff.

As much as you tell yourself it’s just a game etc. this isn’t pleasant. Would letting them push you on to just music be a way out? Or would giving up the ED spot leave you powerless and miserable? Or are you already powerless and miserable?

2021

So in the last couple of days, kind of like the last days of the pandemic for you, you’ve finally had the big idea. And even got the name for it. Yesterday was using simply coloured notation on the staff for the gabaritos (as opposed to a reference at the back of the book). Today was also significant: the idea that the Gabarito isn’t some long scale for looking up the notes - it’s the notes and patterns of the piece condensed as far as possible into a 4 bar phrase which, played in the a given key, sets the scene. Crucially, Katarina had no problem switching between reading off note names and scale degrees. This is big.

Rushed day - didn’t even ring Mum on her birthday. Photographer from Globo came round and got some excellent short of Edileuza and Duda. Running around trying to get as many kids as poss to sign Amelia’a card.

Nice e-mails from Simon Cook.

Kind of packed - still don’t feel confident I have everything under control.

=== 9 October.md ===
# 9 October

9 October

2022

Baile Brass with Os Siderais went well but you felt like crap, largely because you had to deal with Samuel’s Mum kicking off and Samuel going to get his trumpet and threatening that his dad will sue you.  Also found out on later that Lucia told all the other kids her stories about Rafael despite everything.

Cris wants to take the kids to Novo Friburgo which would be great in one way but I’m not sure I can face it at this point. Another sticky executive decision. Lucia shouldn’t have been at the party - that was you going with Cris’s decisions.

You will never be able to get away from Favela Brass politics. Cris will always be able to point at you as the one who decides which kid is in which group etc. But you can get the workload down and take some of the heat off you.

And in the long run, passing on the ED baton puts you on the off-ramp. Gives you more time to focus on getting the musical side less and less dependent on you. If you want to get out, this is the best way without the quality of the teaching suffering.

And here’s the kicker - you’re worried about abandoning the project when there’s a real possibility that it will actually do better without you. Let it fly and take the form that it will.

You will have done 3 years as ED, maybe a realistic goal would be 3 more in a gradually diminishing artistic director role then out.

2020

Fairly solid day. In the morning working on arrangement of Tim Maia’s “Eu não quero dinheiro”. Such a great artist - definitely the first place to look for MPB repertoire. Decided to do it for 3 trumpets and 3 troms. With a pro band you want to keep the numbers down but with the kids surely you want to include as many as possible - especially if it will make it sound better. This also opens up the possibility of Nelsinho-style samba and brass arrangements, with the option of using the sax like the voice, as as “puxador”.

Struggled through with only a green tea for breakfast (made from the leaves for you by the lovely chef at the the Litoral Hotel). Coming off caffeine really does hit you where it hurts. But productive day, got the newsletters off, tied up loose ends, gave lessons to the Marias and João Vitor. PF site not working it would be unfair if they fine you I think.

Teresopolis. It’s raining loads and the clouds are obscuring the views. First restaurant that fishy place where the mad waiter insisted on us trying chopp de vinho and didn’t bring the chips.

Nice hot chocolate place, antique shop and Teresopolis brewery was great. Monique bit drunk and random, back home and played cards.

That is, the one that you didn’t go to because you were too “busy” in Rio and/or were too proud to ask for the plane ticket.

2021

Minor hitch at Charles de Gaulle airport yesterday - Brazil removed the exemption for Brits with permanent residency after the initial announcement on the 23rd of December. This info was only on the English-language side of the Itamatary website but that’s no excuse really - you should have double-checked everything. Only found this out at 23:30 when they didn’t let me get on the flight.

Subsequently ended up sleeping in CDG airport then getting a flight back to Heathrow and currently on a train up to Donny from Kings Cross. This particular debacle has cost you:

1 train ticket to Manchester and two up to Donny from Kings Cross plus tube fare and other bits (say £150).

COVID green-light at home - get back in the garage mate!

£120 of M+Ds money for another PCR test to cut quarantine if you go for it

£120 of your money for another PCR test to get back (assuming you need it when they open up again)

Time

Was very annoyed with myself and generally a bit miserable but a WHSmith meal deal, Costas Cappuchino and a chance to ride in a fairly empty carriage in one of the new Azuma trains has put a better complexion on things. 

To make sense of this you now need to spend the next few weeks working your arse off on the arrangements in the garage. Technically you could spend 14 days in another country and then go to Brazil but seems a little quixotic and expensive. If you were going to go down that route sooner rather than later would make sense.

Does seem like a good excuse to lock yourself in the garage and do arrangements though…

=== April 26.md ===
# April 26

2021

I’m grateful for Bach - that beginner Bach book has been a godsend. Perfect for getting you into improvising baroque melodies and harmonies. The next level of harmonic understanding is all there: just keep hitting the Bach - it’s like a harmony Arban.

I’m grateful for the new bike route going up to the caixa d’água then down via paineras (VERY grateful for that) and also grateful to whoever had the great idea of putting outdoor gym things all over Rio (including on my bike route)

On a more sombre note Dad isn’t well. Mum has sent cash to all his children (likely to be so I can get back in an emergency) and started a WhatsApp group to cover his health. She said he won’t be going abroad any more. Sounds like she’s managing expectations. It’s coming.

Today was the day that I started being able to improvise baroque melodies on trumpet. Something has clicked. It’s wonderful to be making such strides musically on the wrong side of 40.

Had a bit of an anti-Brazil funk today. Maybe I was just down. It just hit me what a selfish, careless, reckless bunch people here are when it comes down to it. And how it has been a bit of a one-handed clap with a lot of parents and kids. 

=== April 27.md ===
# April 27

April 27

2021

Pensive at the moment. Can’t help feeling I let Dad down. No kids, no money, living in a slum in a house they paid for. You brought home a beautiful black girl that he would have loved to have as a daughter. Then dumped her.

He did his bit. He didn’t go around beating his chest doing philanthropic projects with other people’s money because that’s what he thought would make himself happy. His morality was to not drop the ball, to be able to provide for your family. To get on with the stuff of life. The holiday in Italy with the family. Playing duets father and son at the piano.

Spoke to Ed today and he called you on your U-turn about exams (you now have no interest in doing exams for Brazil having previously expounded passionately about it). Flip-flop. 

I’m grateful for having a Dad who could provide for me financially. So many people don’t and I just took it for granted. The music lessons, the instruments, the last 12 years in Brazil. You had it on a plate.

I’m grateful for bolo de aipim and I’m grateful for maple syrup. And for the combination of the two.

=== April 29 2021.md ===
# April 29 2021

It’s all about the patterns. Not short patterns necessarily, better in fact to learn whole tunes. But it’s all about getting those patterns into your head. Those are the fuel. Those are the chess moves. How many cards can you do in a day? Let’s get to 52 a week mate. This is so important- it’s you the musician. Are you going to get to the real top levels or not?

Also I am getting more and more convinced about transposing stuff at the keyboard being the best way to understand it. Chord scale theory or schenkian analysis still can’t capture the whole thing, the ambiguous key centres. If you can hear something, go to the piano and play it in any key, you’ve understood it end of argument. 

Coming back down to earth, literally, I came off the bike yesterday. Wet tram rails - the classic. In a weird way you liked it. Be honest. Taking a proper knock for the first time in a few years - maybe since breaking foot (which was not fun at all).

It’s a fantastic imaginative, productive time. But there’s a creeping loneliness - missing having a girlfriend, sharing life, a lot. 

I am grateful for Tinder. Did I say that already? It got you past your sticking point (approaching girls) there’s no doubt about that. Only today I thought of all amazing the girls I have been with. What a privilege.

I am also grateful for whiteboards to change gears with thinking, and for Hedi’s pizza which I am taking a rain check on for the moment because of COVID.

Mum and Dad just gave you a bunch of cash clearly for you to come back. It’s possible via Mexico but I want to hold the fort with the lessons till the end of June. 

Thinking about writing a brass group arrangement that you could record. It’s a start for the budding composer in you.

=== August 31st 2020.md ===
# August 31st 2020

August 31st 2020

Writing the diary with a beer. This is a novelty.

Oli’s family over the last few days, lovely BBQ yesterday and fun times watching old batman series episodes on Youtube. Just about managed to maintain the 3 hours in the morning on making course materials - recorder karate is well and truly done and now sorting out the melodica course which is already shaping up well.

These last few weeks have been great generally, but the whole Stugger Carola situation has been tricky. This afternoon you’ve had that horrible indecision feeling - tying yourself in knots thinking about the curry that you’re trying to organize for Wednesday as well as getting instruments fixed, how you’re going to do the trip to London and so on.

Just now you were feeling like you HAD to have a drink because you were feeling stressed about all this, but also because that is now the rhythm - after 3 cups of tea life you’re ready for a beer to make yourself feel human again at the end of the afternoon.

Point is, putting off decisions is not good. You end up making bad non-decisions by default and you end up with things dragging on. You have to get yourself out of this habit of turning from decisions. But, in your defence, tricky situation with Stugger and Carola and also Covid. This one with Carola needs thinking over really well now as it now turns out that she has come back from London.

I’m getting bored of this, so I’ll just list the options for now:

1. Fire her after curry. Set up a coffee and then just do it.
2. Fire her before curry.
3. Give her a dressing down now, take her off Rouanet and then wait till there’s a good opportunity.
4. Find stuff for her to do and bide your time.
5. Drop her to half wages
6. Say that you’ll only hire her when you need her.

Considerations

1. Would be good to talk to the board. This really is a good reason to delay - they are what give you legitimacy and the one way to not have them on your side is to do stuff like this without talking to them (but… they might try to block you)
2. Not having been able to talk to the board gives you an excuse to have delayed, as does the fact that her and Stugger are at a very delicate point.
3. You haven’t given her a clear warning, so might seem unfair
4. She is clearly a freelance and doesn’t even have Favela Brass down as her main job
5. Would be good to have her do the donkey work for Rouanet so it actually gets done!
6. You’re paying for the privilege of having your life made difficult.
7. She is taking the place of another person who you could be grooming to take over the development side of things.
8. You should not make big decisions based on what Stugger might say or do.
9. There’s a decent probability of Stugger and Carola falling out again
10. Carola and Stugger both play hard-ball with you. 
11. She’s telling people that you’re crazy and god knows what else, and generally working against you. Remember the 48 laws - you could really come to regret not seizing the moment here. Need to try to get her RIGHT OUT.

But here’s the biggest problem

=== August 3rd 2019.md ===
# August 3rd 2019
In your heart of hearts you know you did the right thing. But... this does leave you with a bit of a mountain to climb. You don’t want to be taking on other people’s children, and you yourself want to have kids. That means dating girls less than 30 years old, and it also means getting to the point where you can commit and start a family in the next few years.

I’ve realized that a part of this is learning to love people’s imperfections. Taking people as they are. Letting things go. You didn’t like Talita’s moments of inflexibility/insensitivity/selfishness, but you yourself most certainly have your inflexible, insensitive, and selfish moments. You can’t be a hypocrite about all this.

I think the thing is that you can’t spend the whole time thinking of why the other person doesn’t measure up. Making your list of things that they said or did that give you grounds for moving on. The primary focus has to be on making the relationship work - can I live with this? You yourself have to be a good boyfriend.

Only now, reflecting, can you see/understand what was at the heart of Talita’s way of doing things: she wants to stick up for herself, and what she thinks is right. She feels the need to defend her rights. As a black, poor woman in a macho society, isn’t that more than understandable?

You need, of course, to find a woman with whom the day-to-day is going to be pleasant, and who is not going to fight you over doing her bit. By the same token you shouldn’t be insisting on a doormat: YOU should be bigger than that.

One thing that became clear as well is that this business of wanting to be free to play the field is rubbish: it’s a happiness trap. Happiness is 1 woman.

 

=== August 5th 2019.md ===
# August 5th 2019
Went out Saturday and drank more than I should have with Tom Le Mesurier. Was good for very little yesterday. Have to stop doing this - just don’t have the time. Alternating alcoholic and non-alcoholic drinks would seem like a good way to put the brakes on things.

Talita asked me if I was sure on Saturday and I replied in the affirmative. One things that you said to Tom seemed to make sense: you wouldn’t do it if things were right. At nearly 40 years old it would seem pretty crazy to be letting a relationship roll on where you are full of doubts. You can never be sure with any decision, but you can feel confident. Marrying Talita was not a prospect that filled you with confidence.

You have already started chatting on Tinder. On the one hand you wan to give yourself time to get over the breakup, and this really has left you down in the dumps and it’s weird how this actually feels like losing a person - like a relative dying. However, on the other hand you have no time to waste.

You had the Favela Brass parents meeting at your house on Saturday morning and only 3 parents went. As a result you cancelled lessons this week and made an ultimatum: come to the meeting next week, arrange another time, or out you go. The problem is parents not taking the project seriously. No responding to Whatsapp messages, and putting other things in front of the project.

What complicates matters slightly is that in 2021 you are going to be starting another set of classes, hopefully at CIEP, which may mean stripping down the course in the favela. To a certain extent, the parents’ lack of support and involvement plays into your hands for doing this. The more you demand of them now, the worse it looks if you later have to strip things down, in order to concentrate on the schools. For now, though, it would seem to make sense to work on what we have, to try and put things right in the knowledge that we can afford to lose students now.

=== August 7th 2019.md ===
# August 7th 2019
Lorena left the project yesterday. The first of the long-standing students to go. At this point there is some serious strategic thinking to be done to make sure that the next phase of Favela Brass is constructed on a solid foundation and wastes neither time nor money.

=== August 8th 2019.md ===
# August 8th 2019
Thinking more seriously about the idea of doing an online iPGCE. With that, your CV starts to look quite good for teaching jobs at international schools. The option of extending it to an MA is also tempting (have to find a way to finance it).

A full-time job at an international school would give you financial security, a good school to send your kids to and also a potential stream of students to join your extra-curricular programs. Indeed, what makes this seem like a viable option is the idea that Favela Brass is moving towards the idea of a 2:30pm - 5:30pm extracurricular band program at CIEP. No reason why private school students couldn’t be a (paying) part of that, or why you couldn’t do the same thing for TBS students on Tuesdays & Thursdays.

Yes, it would mean a lot of time giving lessons for rich kids and less “free” time for self-development. But remember that all teachers have free periods and all you would have to do is buy a laptop. The melodica lessons that currently happen at 12H and 14:30H could be covered by other teachers, so you would be looking at 7:30 - 15H in the schools, followed by 15:30-17:30 at CIEP, then maybe 18:30 - 20:30 in the favela. It’s a lot, but remember all the public holidays, lost days and the fact that it all stops for July and January.

David Brennan made a point about doing things while you have time. At the moment you don’t have kids or a wife - that may not always be the case. It does seem like a good time to do this. Sometimes you just have to move in the right general direction. Take Talita’s advice: get yourself qualified.

=== December 29.md ===
# December 29

DAILY NUGGET

We can’t take anything with us. We can’t leave an immortal legacy. So what does that leave? Living a good, fulfilling life. Doing what feels good - working with other people to achieve worthwhile stuff.

2021

Last night in Lisbon. Gambar the prawn place - very good indeed. Running out of steam by the end of the night. Up very early this morning to fly back Ryanair which is a bit basic. 

Listening to 4,000 weeks still, and still trying to get my head round it. One of the most enjoyable moments of the holiday was obsessively practicing Bach on the battlements of Lisbon castle, contemplating the view.

You like creating, you like developing, you like making music. That feeling of things gradually getting better. Is that “instrumentalizing” your time? What’s the problem if you enjoy it? The whole work/leisure thing is more of a grey area for you.

Oliver Burkemann says that spending all our time working for tomorrow is silly, because we never reach the “promised land”. Well, that may be the case if you’re a lawyer, but as a musician honing his craft, or a teacher getting his band together things are a bit different. There’s a pleasurable rhythm of improvement - “is there somewhere you’d rather be?”

Fact is that we’re all going to go one day and we can’t take any of our achievements with us. But that doesn’t mean that we can’t savor them during our life. Many great things in the book, and yes hobbies and downtime are great, but to say that it doesn’t make much difference what we do with our lives is to downplay the human experience too much.

To make other people’s lives better is meaningful, and human joy and suffering are very real for those who experience them. It starts at home, but yes it is worth working hard to make things better for those around us, even if it won’t last a thousand years. What else do we have?

=== December 6th.md ===
# December 6th

2023

Shitty day yesterday. Gabriel from PRIO casually dropped in that they won’t be giving giving us money until next year, which totally throws a spanner in the works. Really puts the heat on you, because you didn’t arrange other companies.

2. Do absolutely everything to get more money in via rouanet: now the newsletter is out think about WhatsApp groups. Talk to the BCS bods.

4. Get yourself into this conversation with the SME so Cris can’t blindside you again. Then look at leaving the school contacts with Pat as produtora executiva.
5. Calm down. Don’t lash out at any part for all of this. Smile, and keep everyone on board as you do the above. Don’t harass. Don’t complain.

=== June 1st.md ===
# June 1st

2022

Apprehensive reading last year’s diary. You know what’s coming. 

Today was another lazyish day getting over COVID. Fretting over Mum’s birthday present. Lots of Favela Brass stuff ready to bite you in the arse. Send Cris a message saying the project is like a pan of popcorn with the lid off.

Don’t fall out with everyone. Just try to be nice to people. It’s that simple. Work on the anger.

In just call Saul, Nacho gives himself up to save his Dad. Only now do you understand the importance of loyalty.

2021

=== May 10.md ===
# May 10

2021

Just did the whole figurenotes transposing thing with Gabi for the first time. Within about 30 mins she was playing twinkle twinkle in C, F and G, but most importantly, conceptualizing the scale degrees. This is a breakthrough. After all these wacky dead ends, you have something that actually works.

Listening to “responsive teaching”. Interesting this distinction between formative and summarize assessment. If ABRSM are the yearly summative exam, where is the unit-by-unit formative plan?

I’m grateful for great movies, I’m grateful for being able to order cheap fish to the door.

I’m grateful for the amazing world out there to travel. All the incredible cities, foods, views, historic sites that stretch out to infinity.

Saw the Darcy Ribeiro building today with Pam and her architect friend. Walked back with her to her house and talked about the executive director thing. Genie’s out of the bottle now. She’s a bit arrogant, doesn’t have much in the way of charisma, and snarls from time to time. But she’ll be a safe pair of hands for Favela Brass. There’s an aspect of you giving up, but you have to ask yourself: is artistic director and executive director viable as the team grows? Is that really best for the project?

Question is: what’s your niche now? If you’re only doing music at Favela Brass you’ll have a bit of time for a sideline or 2: wouldn’t running a band or two and writing arrangements for them be the ticket? I guess the main thing is getting at the Brassify thing. It’s a good idea. Do it right and it’s bigger than Favela Brass. The world needs it, and it could take you anywhere. Go get ‘em, founder.

# May 14

2024

Can’t believe it’s less than a year since Pam went. At least you did it and got rid of her.

In a mad rush to get the prestação de contas done today in time for the finance meeting, but it’s not work that you don’t like. It’s the politics and the overwhelm that you don’t like.

Just putting the finishing touches to Beyoncé Crazy in Love

2023

Baile Brass yesterday with the Bloco das Tubas. Really low audience turnout - was advertised at the last minute because of delay in confirming the band and approving the flyer. Everyone needs to have a think about how we can get a better turn out at the next one (which involves everyone inviting a few people there, including board). Students played great though and had a good time.

Despite wanting to pass over the reigns to Pam, there is a niggling worry: she can be an arrogant, bossy cow at times and she isn’t treating you with proper respect (same for Viviane). She has already rolled her eyes at you (signalling contempt) in meetings and talks over you. The question is: will this move make things worse or better for you? Are you rushing to get out of a bad, fixable situation but creating a worse, unfixable (or fixable only by you leaving) situation? Or will this dynamic always be there with whoever you get in?

Where do you want to go with this? Last night after the ball Joe and annoying Ukranian Airbnb guest Viktoria were out. You cranked up the hi-fi, nailed some beers, and jammed along on the trumpet: ecstasy. You take pleasure and satisfaction from music. Not from endless team meetings. In your heart, you just want to be creative - to write and record arrangements, and to play great music in public. 

In terms of Favela Brass if you could just teach the top band (including impro), and define the course materials and repertoire that would be grand. There’s some politics in there but nothing you can’t handle. Remember that top band will just get better with time. Other teachers would LOVE to take ownership of a specific bands, and Joe is better than you gave him credit for. One day of teaching in the schools could actually be quite pleasant as well.

This opens the door for you to live outside the favela if want to, maintaining good relations here. And if you ever did want to move somewhere else, you could be employed by Favela Brass to look after their course. Wouldn’t the board love to have you as a prestador de serviços? What about the consultancy thing?

This comes back a bit to the Shimano gears thing - would it be you looking after Favela Brass’s course, or would you be looking after Brassify, which Favela Brass would be using? Would the Shimano gears be the Favela Brass course in other projects, or Brassify in a bunch of projects including Favela Brass?

And coming back to it - it was so nice to be blowing away freely on the trumpet. Not the petty politics. Remember that dream of the white room? That room could be where you live now, or it could be somewhere else. You could invest in a house for Airbnb or… you could just invest the cash and use the interest and rent on your house to get by while you focus on Brassify. The truth is that you have the room you need at least for audio recordings

=== May 15.md ===
# May 15

2024

« Remember that to improve, one must master difficulties each day »
- Herbert Clarke

Started reading the Strive book, which is a good complement to the Becoming Who you Are. Basically, there’s no such thing as a free lunch: you’ll have a better life dealing with unpleasant stuff and putting up with risk.

With Favela Brass it’s a case of working out what the most courageous thing would be: to stick with it, or to go for it with the arrangements. At least the 90 mins per day 6 days a week NO MATTER WHAT is ingrained now, but what if you went at it all day every day for a year? Five years?

Thinking about what would get more people playing your arrangements and coming back to that idea about university students. They’re at the right age and in the states must be plenty of students who could handle the charts because of the whole band program culture. How to get a foot in the door while still living in Engenho do Mato… what can be done online?

In the podcast Adam Fraser talks about how people’s end of life regrets are about not having had the courage to go for it. « It » for you is creating these arrangements with videos. To create the brass band real book.

2022

Rehearsal at CIEP. Trying to work out who to put on what instrument. Zuri wants to do trombone. Great! Vinicio said about tuba but the logistics might be difficult. Maybe do Tpt/Sax/Trom with the pereira brothers.

Really wanted to chill later but had to do Cacilda for a grand total of 2 horns and 3 percussion students. Only me, Dan and the new sax guy (misreal?) later. At least it didn’t cost you more than a few Ubers.

2021

Think you may have found your active recovery activity: working on the house. It works really well to take you away from thinking about syllabuses etc., it combines well with audio books and it is very satisfying to be getting things done. Also great generally to have a nicer, tidier house and also obviously good from a hosting point of view. 

May have hit on the exam format (again) this morning. Just work with the public domain tunes. Stick all the exercises (transposition, variations, etc.) in pdf, support them with references and YouTube playalongs, including whole-exam playalongs. Thing is, this makes it more of a method. Ed won’t like it. The free choice pieces are what make it an exam. But how to support them with accompaniment? Also the trumpet exam pieces on the UK lists seem distinctly uninspiring. The literature just isn’t there.

Tom Le Mesurier got in touch saying he’s had a call ostensibly from the gang that run coroa (TCP?), obviously I couldn’t help directly. Been thinking quite a bit recently about the “situation” here in Pereira: ninguém aceita apanhar.

=== May 23.md ===
# May 23

2023

First cortejo at the Aterro Saturday and Atados DBA with OV at Arpoador Sunday. 

Trying to get Rouanet project approved but Mirela being difficult - starting to think that we need a new president for next year.

Getting more organized and this seems to be helping quite a bit with stress - I just focus on executing the system, rather than getting overwhelmed thinking about all the things that I should be doing. The whole EDP/ADP/EDI/ADI pomodoro cycle thing seems to be a winner when you can get it going.

Thinking a lot about this idea of doing a sabbatical next year. Is it practical? Will the board revolt (Especially Mirela)? Is the team ready (we’re getting to the point where it’s time to resolve the Cris issue)?

The thinking is that only by you leaving will people actually learn to run the day-to-day without you. Then you are able to come back in in a role that you will be able to do forever because it’s not going to burn you out or drive staff nuts. Writing arrangements, rehearsing the main band, organising the curriculum.

Can it run without you? The secret sauce is the arrangements and the syllabus. And those will only get better with you away from the day to day.

Another way is for next year you to get away just from the day to day - to go straight to the role that you wanted to go to after the year out. Maybe you could still move away, but come back for the weekends for Friday’s rehearsal, the Aterro and the shows if needed (Fri/Sat). Where to sleep Friday night?

Coming back to this… the big question is whether you can trust Pam with the project. She’s just not that nice. It’s a gamble - she’s efficient and strict with staff, but she’s got you looking at the door. To be fair you were already looking at the door. She’s now working on cutting Cris out of the project, stripping her of her duties at the aterro, getting an admin assistant in to learn her job. Feels a bit like you set a rottweiler on Cris - and yourself. Do you want a rottweiler running Favela Brass?

She’s arrogant and demeaning, with a hint of contempt. Can you leave someone like that at the wheel? 

2022

Paraty was a great success. Kids absolutely nailed it and you really enjoyed it - maybe this is the way you travel in Brazil. Slightly worried that the festival might be a bit threatened by the way the kids outshined the rest of it, but it’s hard to imagine us not getting a bunch of great stuff off the back of this.

Now for the bad bit. You were caffeinated and gave out some pretty heavy-handed and unfair bollockings. First the sax player Dudu for leading you the wrong way with the bloco, then with Alexandre at the end of the bloco for trying to keep the kids playing. Then finally Camila twice on the last day for the kids putting stickers on their instruments and getting involved production decisions with Robert.

To be fair, the situation with Robert was annoying, but you didn’t exactly handle it with aplomb - quite the opposite. Too much caffeine and not enough sleep. Shades of TBS. Carry on like this and you’re going to lose all your friends. There will always be a bunch of stuff to do. Cut the caffeine out now.

Turma 1 students are really excited to play now. Great energy in the lesson today. Thinking about doing a bloco/orquestra/banda division mon/wed/fri. Need to think all this through tomorrow…

Back to the red card?

Came to the conclusion yesterday morning that Pam has to go because she’s not up to the Ed role - mainly because she’s a massive cow. Who is going to want to deal with her? “Eu não tenho incremento” and the whole business of wanting to inform PRIO that we won’t do any more shows with less than 2 weeks notice.

After an almost sleepless night spoke to Melissa, Sômulo, Mirela and Lucca with a view to firing her, but only Melissa has the stomach for it.  And we come back to the situation than they won’t accept Favela Brass without me reporting to the board.

You need to calm down and work out the strategy here: you want to get favela brass to the point where it’s running without you, but you’re still organizing the course and the arrangements. 

Chatted with Lucca about how to get you out of the day to day - and all these meetings. The Rouanet dúvidas meetings, meetings about the logistics of the festa junina, activities planning for the month. The idea of all this was to have someone to handle just the Rouanet project. 

You need to be USING Pam. She’s a great cat’s paw and she can handle the day to day.0

If you’re going to stay above Pam you need to avoid being in meetings as musical director. Do you put someone else in for this? Do you need someone else to be in charge of rehearsing the band and doing shows full time?

You need to get to a point where it’s the others who are running ragged and not you. 

The other thing that crossed your mind is handing your notice in. But what is difficult with that is: who hires the next project coordinator? Isn’t that the board? Or is that your role?

It’s like you almost have to care less about the project.

Ok so here’s the key insight: the ideal is you creating great materials and giving the lessons. The next best is you creating great materials and other people giving the lessons. Yesterday you didn’t have the materials you needed for the lesson and that weighed more than you being there or not to give the lessons.

If you have a cool new arrangement with supporting videos and people to work on it with the students isn’t that enough? If you have a thorough curriculum with exams and method books isn’t that enough? Joe’s your go-to guy for this. Give him the setlist and off you go. And this goes for shows as well. Any teacher should be able to take a band to a show and pick a setlist.

2022

Reading last year’s entry and can’t help hearing the old man’s words: keep your feet on the ground. You nailed Paraty musically but you didn’t keep calm. If you’re going to lead this thing, even with a light touch, you’d better be the one calming other people down.

While we’re at it if you’re so thin skinned, then wouldn’t it make sense to be sensitive with other people’s feelings? It all just comes back at you with interest. Work on the hearts and minds of others.

Enjoyable day working on princesa arrangement, meetings etc. Brain definitely not working well though.

Lucia tested positive for COVID and looks like Cris and Hedi have COVID so cancelled the gigs off this weekend. Would have been a shitshow without you anyway.

2021

Creeping little victories with the method (thinking Favela Brass method is the brand and maybe your escape from being ED in a few years could possibly be spreading the method abroad). New way of presenting transposing version with computer notes on single live stave looks good, as does the coloured static harmony representation.

Finally finished the guri recordings. There aren’t as many of them as there could have been and they aren’t that good. But it’s done. There is a lot to be said for working through written arrangements but I prefer doing transposable tunes, harmonies backings plus rhythm reading warmups for each tune (another innovation today).

I am grateful for the opportunity to make so much of a difference in Rio. This could really be transformative for the city. It’s very exciting and never forget whatever the wrinkles you have the main thing that most people never have - a purpose.

I am grateful for my kindle to read books like the Lisbon history I just downloaded, and I am grateful for the art of manliness podcast and it’s nicely varied selection of topics and interviewees - perfect for cycling up a hill with!

Remember that vídeo? You are doing something that requires courage. 

Are you a fantasist? Or can you plant you feet somewhere and make stuff happen? 

Quality of life indexes mean nothing. Look at Amelia - flitting away, wants to do ethnomusicology to visit all these other countries. But where’s the purpose? Means nothing.

It’s all about the meaning. 

Question has been asked though. If the ideal thing is handing the ED role of favela brass off, what would you afterwards? Don’t have to leave Brazil, don’t have to leave favela brass but what would you do? What would you want to do?

As it was it was you and regivaldo with flimsy masks on taking the stuff out, shortly after it happened and you’re still living in the house. I guess just get the roof sorted, clean the shit out of the house and forget about it.

Booked the epic trip back via Mexico and NYC. Also came up with exam format of just technical studies and transposition. Also thought about possibility of selling books on teachers pay teachers. Nathan did the first page of transposition using Figurenotes yesterday and this is clearly the way.

=== November 10th.md ===
# November 10th

November 10th

2020

Money. Listened to the Morgan Housel, author of The Psychology of Money on the Art of Manliness podcast on Sunday and have had it at the back of my mind since. The iron rule for wealth is to “Live within your means and be patient.” and the key thing is to start saving early, ideally from age 10 like Warren Buffet. Great. At 41 without savings or a decent income the best I can say is that at least I have a house (that I didn’t earn). Technically, I could go indefinitely with both rooms rented out.

In your late twenties you read The Millionaire Next Door and Rich Dad, Poor Dad. You knew. Problem was that you just didn’t have the income over expenses until starting at the British School. From 2017 you could have saved money though. Think about the trips to America and Europe. All those meals out. Also the slowness to get the new house up to scratch and rented. And now you’ve quit the British School and turned down the American School.

So other than printing out the cashflow quadrant and sticking it under your glass desk, what can you do now? Been listening to Marco Pierre White and Gordon Ramsey making huge sums of money. You don’t need all that, but you need to get going. Maybe it’s a bit more simple - maybe you just need to get some decent cash into Favela Brass, do a great job as ED and ask for a decent salary in return. Live within your means, save 10% of your income and invest time and money into income bearing assets, like rental property in Rio.

You spent your 20s looking at your belly button and your 30s having the time of your life in Rio. Point is, you have to be realistic about where your choices have left you. In many ways they have left you in a fantastic place - so much freedom, so much fun to be had in Rio, such an amazing project. But they also mean that you’re kind of committed. You have to run with this now. No more dreaming of landing a cushy job in academia or making a billion dollar app. You have to think that Executive (and musical )Director of Favela Brass is the best (and most important) job in the world, and you have to realise that crushing the job that you are doing is the best thing you can do for your future, financial and otherwise. I.e. Love the one you’re with.

That said… if the key is getting cash into Favela Brass, then how are you going to do that? Rouanet, editais, UK Charity status etc. But how are you going to build the giving network to hit the really big donors. Again it’s about doing the simple things well. Thankyous, newsletters, well thought-out fundraisers. Great performances by the kids in the right places and plenty of videos on Social Media. You also have to say yes to stuff, to push past the fear, to be a bit bold in terms of getting the kids noticed. You also need to take the initiative and build a team. Stop being a perfectionist about this. Look around you - who can take stuff on? Amelia, Joe, Raissa, Dan Lassen. Think! 

Also be strategic. Get these partnerships with the private schools going, including Leandro’s. Use the arrangements to structure exchanges and start a little youth brass movement. That first 90 minutes on arranging is the most important time, the wildly important time. That’s where the musical vision is laid out. That’s the part that only you in the whole world can do. And once an arrangement is done it’s done. Once a body of arrangements is done it’s done, giving every brass band in the world a blueprint to follow.

And maybe if you do get Favela Brass working like a well-oiled machine, if instead of looking for a way around you go straight through, then maybe in a few years time you’ll be able to hand over the reins to capable lieutenants and pursue another related option that presents itself to you. But you have to make Favela Brass a success first, to establish it. This is your calling card, your passport, whatever you want to call it.  

2019

Crazy day yesterday. Met a very crazy and sexy girl called Hinali off tinder for a suco date at 7:30 in the morning, then give lesson at CIEP, then did British School show at Barra, then the lanterna festival at the German school. All went well and Hinali is currently asleep in my bed in her knickers.

The British School plan for next year should be a big concert at both site for Class 3, followed by the opportunity to sign up for the band program premium course. Maybe R$50 - R$100 to have the melodica/perc lessons after school. Kids do end of term shows with Favela Brass and also TBS events.

When the students hit class 4 if they want to continue with the BPP they pay a little more and have private lessons on tpt/trom/sax with the Band Program teachers. This would create a differential within the C4 band program, but the dynamic could be one of the premium students helping the others.

The could move you a step further towards where you want to be: running Rio de Janeiro’s music service. Time to put all this on paper then present it to Melissa, Jose Costa and senior management, and then PTA. Then just need to get out of normal C4 band lessons.

=== November 14th.md ===
# November 14th

2020

Results for the Fomento à Todas as Artes (R$50.000) came out and we placed 26 out of about 200 (only 20 get the cash). Looks like we got a perfect score for everything except location. Will try to do an appeal but seems unlikely. Made the mistake of splashing it around the diretoria group - it’s good to feed them the big news items, but the risk is of you looking needy, or of them getting involved.

In general you need to stop leaking. Stop blabbing. Stop coming across as needy. Stop giving things away. Remember law 4:

“When you are trying to impress people with words, the more you say, the more common you appear, and the less in control. . . The more you say, the less likely you are to say something foolish.”

Also, there’s this poem that Rockefeller, who was famously quiet in meetings, used to quote, apparently:

“There was an owl liv'd in an oak
The more he heard, the less he spoke
The less he spoke, the more he heard.
O, if men were all like that wise bird”

(From Punch, 1875)

Take the example of Marco Pierre White. To uphold standards and discipline you can’t be a lightweight piece of fluff. You need to plant you feet and hold the line. You need to develop habits around this.

Didn’t drink the whisky last night and slept MUCH better. Straight through 10 - 5 with the ear protectors on.

=== November 15th.md ===
# November 15th

Did a bit of preparing teaching slides for the first time in ages. Went back into David Newell’s rhythm teaching book and it clicked - that 1-i-and-a system is the way to go because it ties syllables in with the actual counting of beats. He explains why it’s better than du tá de ta and you only understood this time.

On the morning walk refined the idea of having them practice rhythms at the start of lessons that will prepare them for the graded sign reading tests. So all you need is the slides and the graded sight reading studies. Although you could put videos together later as well.

Norton and co came round for lunch at abcd. Went fine - it does seem like they are connected, but they are also new to captação, and to you. Have to avoid paying them commission for our donors. Fátima is saying the next project shouldn’t be 1 million but that we should work up to it. Makes sense.

New series of the crown on Netflix. Episode about Mountbatten’s death got you thinking about Dad. That’s going to be very tough when it comes. I don’t like the idea of him not seeing his grandkids. Like I let him down, and Mum as well. This part of your life has to move forward.

Mad scramble yesterday to get signatures to prove you have students outside of centro/zona sul, as an appeal against our 2/5 points for location in the fomento às artes grant (R$50k). Unlikely to change anything but still, very happy that they scored the rest of our application 20/20.

In the evening went out for pizza and drinks in Leblon with Kenny and Joe. Was really nice to get out. Kenny is a great person to have as a friend. Exactly the kind of guile-less person that the existentialism guy Robert Marino was talking about on the Art of Manliness podcast. Look after this friendship. All cool with joe at the mo as well.

=== November 17th.md ===
# November 17th

2023

Playing music as a hobby. If you want a great leisure activity you don’t need to look further than working on Bach chorales through the keys at the piano. When you were a kid school was work and you managed to do a lot of practice once school was over (or before school). You would write music weekends and evenings and it wasn’t work. Now you’ve found the first 90 minutes of the day for writing which is great and I guess that’s half work. Trumpet and piano (and sax and trombone and whatever instruments you want to learn) should feel like hobbies. Practice can still be rigorous and scheduled - you can still stretch -  but somehow it has to feel like leisure. Nothing sorts your head out like a couple of hours at the piano.

2020

I think we can call today a draw. Very lethargic in the morning and even ended up napping but still got stuff done and didn’t eat too much which was good. Hit the basics - meditation, workout, piano, trumpet and meeze - and the rest is a bonus. Also hit on a good routine of finishing at 6pm and then walking down to Flamengo beach and then back up via Santa Teresa whilst listening to potential tunes for the brass band.

# November 26th

November 26th

2019

Great talk yesterday with Ed Matkin. Takeaways were:

1. Rouanet will involve massive amounts of paperwork - need to pay Carola to handle that full-time.
2. He has a “puppet” board of 10 chums rather than a proper one - your project will have a differential.
3. You must keep your nose clean, cross all your t’s and dot all your i’s because at some point somebody is going to come for you.
4. Sign-off is the important thing when delegating. Need to keep produtoras on a short leash.
5. Other states seem to have bands in the schools - Rio is unusual.
6. Avoid getting entangled with politicians at all costs - must stay independent.

Also chatted to Bill Ballantayne and he’s up for a chat about setting up our board. Seeing Sandra later today to talk about the whole board thing. More than a little worried that she’s going to be crazy at board meetings/overbearing. Perhaps not the best choice with hindsight.

Have booked a whole table for the TBS Christmas Celebration. Pricey, but good to be able to show the FB team that I value their work, and to be seen to be contributing to the BCS. Since the proceeds from the event got to us it ends up being a donation to Favela Brass anyway…

# 2020

Medium day. Finished Shining Lights (which I think could be my first decent brass band arrangement) and got stuck into Odara. Right now finishing a decent brass band arrangement feels like the best result to have in my hand at the end of a day.

Having an eerie feeling about what it will be like to write this diary in 2060. That day will come, you will be writing that diary. Not only that, you will be reading this one. === November 4th 2020.md ===
# November 4th 2020



November 4th 2020

Favelagrafia want to do a recording with the kids. They want 10 kids from turma 1 to record a tune somewhere in a favela, but then it starts to become unclear.

It’s something to do with a commercial for Boticário but he’s saying that the commercial has already been made and this is an “acao em conjunto”. When I asked about COVID he said we’d be wearing gloves.

When I asked about cash they said there would be money for the kids. Didn’t even consider the possibility that the project should get some cash. And they have started by talking to the lads in fogueteiro and saying there might be cash which doesn’t help.

Also the reference they sent was when you wish upon a star with Louis Armstrong which is all strings and vocal. Some of silly talk about “abrindo vozes” and assuming that I will do an arrangement for free. And the magic line about exposure for the project.

All in all not ideal but 2 problems for dismissing it: wouldn’t be good for relationship with kids in Fogueteiro or with Favelagrafia (who have already done us a favor), local project etc. Also, it’s you saying no to stuff, holding the project back from doing stuff.

Very tempted to just recommend them a string project in the nicest possible way. Would be nice to help them, but once we’ve said yes I’m worried they will take the piss in terms of COVID and how long we have to play for. And also, is this really going to work?

So there you have it. A nice juicy leader’s dilemma. Enough to stress you out and mess with your sleep last night. Mental note: you hate this stuff.

End of day update: you turned it around. Came up with the idea of sexta básicas to avoid the money issues, wrote the arrangement, set the location, spoke to the parents. Mental note: you love this stuff.

November 4th 2019

Blue Note finally paid so I’m ok for cash. Part of me thinks I should have got out of the British School this year. Financially it’s doable now. Trying to think of a project for next year that could get me working in a better capacity with the British and American schools. Carnival melodica and percussion blocos. Paid extra-curricular activity? (they might take it more seriously if they pay)

Saturday was Amit’s fun run at the Lagoa. As predicted hardly anyone participated (BCS demographics), but it was good networking. Nice to have a beer with Amit and Bill afterwards.

Friday took Joy to Bar dos Descasados. She’s obviously very sexual - i.e. likes sex! And although she has clearly been reading from the same hymn sheet as Talita in terms of feminism etc.. she is a lot more chilled out and cooperative, which was the point all along.

Yesterday picket up bracelets from Alison Correa and asked her if she wants to be on the board for Favela Brass which she didn’t seem to be sure about. Then went to Santa Teresa with Kenny to try and get a gig at Favela Hype but the manager wasn’t there. Life is good.

=== November 8th.md ===
# November 8th

2022

Rewatched Midnight in Paris. I can’t remember if I got before how in the end Gil finds love in the present and not the past once he stops trying to escape it, but I realize now what an effect the film had on you at the time - and its continuing relevance for you. 

The thing is that we really are in a time of cultural stagnation now - nothing of note has happened musically in the last 20 years. That’s your purpose right there - to do something to move the dial on that. You’re never going to bring back the Jazz age, but you could get people playing the latest hits in the street, and you can get some very cool funk brass culture going in the favelas.

An interesting aha moment when Robert Greenberg said that the invention of amplified music had profound consequences - including the death of mass amateur live music-making. Isn’t that what is coming back in Rio? You can’t have a (good) bloco without people playing instruments.

Another aha moment is this thing about hiring people to execute your projects. Almost a franchise-type thing. Can almost imagine Favela Brass taking other projects over. Think Napoleon just giving his groups of troops objectives then letting them attain them in the best way they think possible.

Ah and we got approval for Lei Rouanet today. 

2020

Recording of “When you wish upon star” with kids for Favelagrafia today. Went absolutely fine. Kids played ok not perfect from a COVID perspective but certainly nothing to keep you awake at night. Lots of other kids in the quadra - definitely good for getting them interested.

Did mess up on the logistics front. No water for the kids and the toilet at the Quadra didn’t work. You have to be looking out for the kids all the time, they are the important ones for the project. Now Gabi is back in the project the complainers are back don’t give them anything to whinge about.

Been thinking that the daily burner might be a good approach. Guess the problem is there are too many burners but should be able to whittle it down. 

Long walk today and after I came back on the road, after practicing trumpet on the rock, a group of cyclists were looking at me. They had seen the trumpet and had realised that it was me playing before. Told me how the sound echoed round the whole area and how much they liked it. Was so nice to hear 

2019

Been quite stressed about Carola the last few days. To put it bluntly, she’s generally been a bit bossy without necessarily having the instincts and commitment to let me hand off things to her. Things that would be simple to to resolve with Joe become interminable - plus, email lists, event planning. The tendency is to be putting things on paper that don’t happen, and to end up with a Google Drive full of documents that are out of date or forgotten before they are ever used.

The title of “produtora”seems to imply the person responsible for setting out and elaborating a project. The title of director seems to overlap this a lot. Perhaps approval is a useful tool here: as director, you need the board to approve your plan; as produtora, whatever Carola does should need to be approved by you.

Putting Sandra on the board might not have been the smartest move because a) she is buddies with Carola (who latched on to her at the last Curry) and b) she likes to use her money as an instrument of power.

Perhaps the line for the board is this: I need to delegate many of the functions of Favela Brass. However, one function that I cannot delegate is the coordination of the delegation process. We want Carola in charge of projects, but not the project.

=== October 17th.md ===
# October 17th
Discovered a great book today via the AOM podcast: Work Clean by Dan Charnas, all about applying the principle of mise en place that chefs learn to other working situations. Have spent pretty much all day (post arranging time) listening to it and making notes. A lot rings true about the importance of process tasks. Really want to use it to make a change and get organized.

In tidying up files I saw the reams that I had written about MLT. Not entirely time wasted, but you took all that stuff far too seriously for far too long. 

=== October 18th, 2020 - Aracaju.md ===
# October 18th, 2020 - Aracaju

October 18th, 2020 - Aracaju

This is why the Mise en Place philosophy is so important:

Think of all the time you spent trying to find the educational equivalent of the “lost chord” with 3-4 hours of MLT noodling every day first thing - your best time. All those unfinished files, all those turma 1 rehearsals with no new tunes and all that working for free because you hadn’t taken care of the business and outreach side of things. Not to mention the mess. And leaving Talita in bed alone on Sunday mornings.

Part of the problem was being taken in by MLT itself, but part of the problem was also not prioritizing activities with an eye to what is expected as part of YOUR JOB. *Deep Work *is a great book, but it works as a philosophy for one part of your job - the immersive work. For you to be on top of things - which is really what you want, and what everyone else expects of you - you have to adjust the ratio of immersive and process work in your schedule to achieve that. 

And perhaps even more important you have to think about how you want to live you life. If you had to say whether you have been working clean or dirty these last 6 years, you would have to say that you have been working dirty, and your physical spaces reflect this. Your reputation also reflects this. You are in a situation where you have to have your sh*t together before you can start thinking about doing the creative stuff. 

This year was supposed to be about the management side of things and the mise en place approach is your ticket to getting out of the weeds. Did the first mise yesterday at 16:30, just tidied the hotel room up, but it’s a start, a commitment. Let’s do this!


=== October 21st.md ===
# October 21st

October 21st 

Back in Rio now and enjoying getting down to business with the new mise en place approach. Spent the morning tidying and setting up my station, then the afternoon at the Banco do Brasil with Márcia trying to get to the point where I can make payments from the internet banking (with mixed success). Liking the system whereby I have 7 Favela Brass “burners” on the go at once - one for each aspect of the job.

Almost feeling disillusioned with the Deep Work philosophy that you took to heart so much. The thing is that in fact the one big amazing thing that is wildly important here is the success of Favela Brass, which depends you getting organised and keeping all the plates in the air. Not long interrupted stretches of time going deep into one thing. Of course you need this time, but don’t fetishise it - look at what’s expected of you in your job and get it done whatever it is.

Maybe in 10 years time you will be an academic, or an arranger. But right now you’re a coordinator first.

=== October 29th.md ===
# October 29th

October 29th

2019

Up at 4 today (with the help of coffee). Really wanting to leave the British School - yesterday was so nice with time at home to get on top of Favela Brass Stuff. Kenny has put in a good word for me at the American school, but they told him I wasn’t qualified, basically. However, looks like I’ll get an interview.

A feeder system of melodica and percussion into a Saturday morning oficina would be the best. Or melodicas feeding into extra-curricular private lessons and a weekly after-school band.

The opportunity of a pro brass band has to be pursued, and with zeal. This is your career path for your kids, and motivation for older kids to practice. It is also your ticket for promoting live music, and for your own artistic expression. This should be a good 50% of it for you. The question is whether to hire a manager or do the production in house.

Private lessons on Mondays in Pereira are making a lot of sense. The 3-contact model is a good one - private (or at least homogenous) lesson, group rehearsal, and keyboard/melodica + theory lesson.
